# Decisions Channel

Record approved decisions and scope changes.

Use this format:

- Decision ID:
- Requested By:
- Approved By:
- Decision:
- Impacted Milestones:
- Risk Notes:
- Effective Date:

- Decision ID: DEC-0001
- Requested By: Human (project owner, source of truth)
- Approved By: Human (project owner, source of truth)
- Decision: The in-scope debug/trace/parity capability in `agent-protocol/project-baseline.md` (full state dump of CPU/DRAM/SRAM/VRAM, execution-event logs under `debug/traces/` and `debug/logs/`, subfolders under `debug/` for frames/events/audio, plus the `tools/` converters such as memory->png/audio) is confirmed as committed scope and is assigned to a new milestone **M10 — Debug/Trace Infrastructure & openMSX Opcode-Trace Parity**. M10 owns: (a) the CPU trace-export facility, (b) full machine slot/RAM/SRAM/VRAM wiring sufficient to run a comparable openMSX program, and (c) the openMSX opcode-trace / per-instruction parity harness. Milestone **M9** QA blocker **R5** (openMSX opcode-trace parity evidence), which QA rated a CONDITIONAL PASS in `docs/m9-qa-signoff.md` (REQ-M9-010), is formally DEFERRED to M10. R5 is therefore an accepted (deferred), non-fabricated risk for M9 rather than an open coding gap: M9's Z80A opcode-family coverage and interrupt architecture are complete and test-backed (`ctest` 21/21). M9 remains open until the human explicitly requests closure; upon that request M9 may be closed on the strength of this deferral, with R5 tracked to M10. M9 A/B parity evidence therefore remains outstanding-but-accepted and must be delivered under M10 before M10 itself can close.
- Impacted Milestones: M9 (R5 deferred/accepted), M10 (new milestone owning debug/trace/parity implementation).
- Risk Notes: Deferral must not be read as a waiver of correctness — opcode-family and interrupt behavior remain green and verified. R5 parity remains a real, required deliverable under M10; no parity result is to be claimed until a genuine trace-diff harness produces one. Blocker documented in `docs/m9-qa-signoff.md`: openMSX requires full slot/RAM wiring (unmapped 0xC000 reads back 0xFF at reset; headless debugger `step` does not advance PC) and this emulator lacks a trace-export facility — both are M10 scope.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-06

- Decision ID: DEC-0002
- Requested By: Human (project owner) via `/msx-autopilot target=M12` directive on 2026-07-06 requesting three next subsystem milestones labeled "M10 chipset / M11 memory / M12 VDP".
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), interpreting the human directive against the append-only authoritative ledger.
- Decision: The label **M10 is already consumed** by the closed "Debug/Trace Infrastructure & openMSX Opcode-Trace Parity" milestone (`agent-protocol/state/milestones.md`, closed REQ-M10-009). The append-only ledger cannot be rewritten. The human's three requested work items are therefore allocated to the next free IDs, preserving the requested substance and ordering exactly (only the numeric label shifts +1): **M11 = S1985 "MSX-ENGINE" chipset + full system bus + system integration**; **M12 = RAM/VRAM/ROM memory devices + system integration**; **M13 = V9958 VDP + system integration**. Each milestone carries: system integration (wiring into bus/CPU), system-wide unit tests, an openMSX A/B trace-diff, and a required QA sign-off before closure. Sequencing is strict: M11 → M12 → M13 (bus/slot infrastructure precedes the memory devices that populate slots, which precede the VDP that plugs into the I/O bus).
- VRAM placement ruling (human explicitly delegated this judgment): the **128 KB VRAM is owned by the V9958 VDP device**, NOT modeled as an independently CPU-addressable memory region. On real HB-F1XV hardware and in openMSX (`references/openmsx-21.0/src/video/`) the CPU reaches VRAM only through VDP ports `#98/#99`; VRAM has no place in the CPU slot/address map. Consequently the inert `vram_` placeholder currently in `src/machine/hbf1xv_machine.*` (added under M10-S2 as pure storage) migrates into the VDP device in **M13**. M12's memory scope is the CPU-addressable store: 64 KB main RAM (mapper, openMSX slot 3-0) + the ROM set (32 KB BIOS/BASIC, 16 KB SUB, 16 KB KANJI, 16 KB DISK per the Target Machine Specification). Final source placement (folders/files under `src/`) is delegated to the planner with authority to add/rearrange per `src/CLAUDE.md` boundary rules.
- S1985 architecture ruling: per the S1985 fact-sheet §10 (`references/fact-sheets/Yamaha S1985 MSX-ENGINE Chipset.md`) and openMSX (`references/openmsx-21.0/src/MSXS1985.*`, `DeviceFactory.cc`), the engine is NOT a monolith. M11 implements the residual engine-specific behavior as a thin S1985 layer — 16-byte backup RAM on switched-I/O device ID `0xFE`, mapper-readback base `0x80` mask `0x1F` (`100xxxxx`), port mirrors `#98-9B`→`#9C-9F` and `#A8-AB`→`#AC-AF`, the +1 M1 (opcode-fetch) wait state, and VDP `/CSR`/`/CSW` strobe timing — over independent modules (PPI/i8255 slot select, MapperIO) as the planner scopes them. Full PSG/YM2149 and RTC/RP5C01 device internals are their own later milestones (baseline lists psg/rtc separately); M11 provides only the bus/engine seams they will plug into unless the planner justifies including a module. No `references/openmsx-21.0/` or `references/sdl3/` code may be copied into `src/` (GPL isolation, guardrails).
- Impacted Milestones: M11 (new — chipset + system bus), M12 (new — RAM/VRAM/ROM memory), M13 (new — V9958 VDP). No change to closed M0–M10.
- Risk Notes: The human's spoken labels (M10/M11/M12) are remapped to (M11/M12/M13); all downstream artifacts use the new IDs (`docs/m11-*`, `docs/m12-*`, `docs/m13-*`). VDP (M13) is one of the most complex chips in the system; the planner must decompose it into deterministic slices and MUST NOT claim A/B parity without a genuine captured trace-diff (guardrails, DEC-0001 precedent). VRAM-under-VDP means M12 A/B parity is scoped to CPU-visible RAM/ROM only; VRAM parity is M13 scope.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-06
- SUPERSEDED IN PART by DEC-0003 (2026-07-06): the memory and VDP milestones are renumbered (memory M12->M13, VDP M13->M14) to make room for a newly inserted M12 = Z80A CPU parity review. The VRAM-owned-by-VDP and S1985-thin-layer rulings in this DEC-0002 remain in force; only the numeric labels for the memory and VDP milestones change. Read "M12 memory" as M13 and "M13 VDP" as M14 in the text above.

- Decision ID: DEC-0003
- Requested By: Human (project owner) on 2026-07-06: "shift currently planned M12 to M13, M13 to M14 ... insert new M12 to run comprehensive review of current cpu implementation against references/fact-sheets/Zilog Z80A CPU.md and references/openmsx-21.0/ and ensure ours implements it with end-to-end parity ... you get my go upon 100% passing of all unit and system integration tests with zero regression from M1-M12, i grant you to close. after M12 is closed, then move onto M13 (Memory related)."
- Approved By: Human (project owner, source of truth) — standing directive.
- Decision: (1) RENUMBER the two Planned-but-unstarted milestones: the RAM/ROM memory milestone moves M12 -> **M13**, and the V9958 VDP milestone moves M13 -> **M14**. (2) INSERT a new **M12 = Z80A CPU End-to-End Parity Review & Hardening (HB-F1XV Zilog NMOS)**: a comprehensive review of the current CPU implementation (`src/devices/cpu/*`, built in M9) against `references/fact-sheets/Zilog Z80A CPU.md` and openMSX (`references/openmsx-21.0/src/cpu/CPUCore.cc`, `CPURegs.cc`, `Z80.hh`) to establish end-to-end behavioral + timing parity for a genuine Zilog NMOS Z80A. If a distance from spec is found, plan -> implement -> test to close it; if already at parity, prove it with targeted parity tests. Full system integration test required (CPU exercised through the M11 system bus, not just in isolation). (3) New execution order: M11 (done) -> M12 (CPU parity) -> M13 (memory) -> M14 (VDP). (4) src/ placement stays under `src/devices/cpu/`; the planner may reorganize/add files (flag tables, undocumented-op modules, etc.) with best judgment per `src/CLAUDE.md`.
- CLOSE AUTHORIZATION (standing): the coordinator is GRANTED authority to CLOSE M12 WITHOUT a further human release decision, conditioned strictly on: 100% pass of ALL unit AND system-integration tests, with ZERO regression across the M1–M12 suites, and a QA sign-off recommending Pass. If that bar is not fully met (any failing/skipped test, any regression, or QA anything less than Pass), M12 does NOT auto-close and the coordinator escalates to the human. This grant applies to M12 ONLY; M13 and M14 retain the normal human-release-decision gate unless separately granted.
- Impacted Milestones: M12 (new — CPU parity, auto-close-authorized on the 100%/zero-regression bar), M13 (was M12 — memory), M14 (was M13 — VDP). M11 and earlier unaffected (M11 remains closed at tag v1.0.11).
- Risk Notes: All downstream artifacts for the renumbered milestones use the NEW ids (`docs/m13-*` for memory, `docs/m14-*` for VDP); `docs/m12-*` is now the CPU-parity milestone. The M9 CPU core already passed QA as non-stub with complete opcode families + interrupt architecture; M12 is a parity-hardening pass focused on undocumented/NMOS-exact behavior and MSX timing, NOT a rewrite — scope control applies (no gratuitous refactor). No A/B parity claim without a genuine captured trace-diff (guardrails). The M11 forward-obligation "flip reset slot default #A8=0xFF -> #A8=0 once ROMs populate slot 0" now belongs to the memory milestone at its new id M13 (not the CPU-parity M12).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-06

- Decision ID: DEC-0004
- Requested By: MSX QA Agent (recommended in docs/m12-qa-signoff.md) + coordinator
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator) under normal scope-tracking authority; not a scope expansion.
- Decision: The Z80A HALT-R behavior (gap #34: on the real Z80 the R register continues to increment while the CPU is halted, since HALT internally re-executes NOP M1 fetches) is formally DEFERRED as an accepted, tracked residual. Rationale: implementing it would alter the QA-signed `hbf1xv_cpu_step` timing oracle and the machine elapsed-cycle accounting, which is out of the parity-hardening scope of M12 and would require re-baselining a signed oracle. It is NOT required by any M12 acceptance criterion and does not affect ZEXALL-class correctness. Tracked as a candidate future timing-fidelity item (companion to DP-4 exact cycle/wait-state timing).
- Impacted Milestones: M12 (closed with #34 accepted-deferred), future timing-fidelity milestone (owner of #34).
- Risk Notes: Deferral is not a correctness waiver — #34 affects only halted-state R-register/refresh timing, invisible to normal instruction-stream execution and to the ZEXALL rubric. Revisit when exact cycle/T-state timing (DP-4) is scoped.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-06

- Decision ID: DEC-0005
- Requested By: Human (project owner) on 2026-07-06: "keep all of which you mentioned deferred item PSG, or RTC ... FM-PAC internals + MSX-JE SRAM, Kanji-font #D8-DB I/O, Halnote firmware, cartridge loading, FDC drive mechanics, and VRAM/VDP (M14) recorded for later milestone reference for planner so no one misses a bit."
- Approved By: Human (project owner, source of truth).
- Decision: Establish `agent-protocol/state/deferred-backlog.md` as the AUTHORITATIVE registry of deferred-but-committed scope. Every future planner package MUST consult it and explicitly state which backlog items the milestone closes and re-affirm the remainder as still-open; the coordinator marks an item DONE (Mxx) in the same cycle it closes (rows are never deleted — history is preserved). Nothing in the backlog is a scope waiver; each item is committed scope from the project baseline / Target Machine Specification, merely sequenced later. The initial registry captures the human-listed items (PSG, RTC, FM-PAC internals + MSX-JE SRAM, Kanji-font #D8-DB I/O, Halnote firmware, cartridge loading, FDC drive mechanics, VRAM/VDP->M14) plus other known deferrals from M9-M13 (exact cycle timing DP-4, HALT-R #34 per DEC-0004, ZEXALL sweep, S1985 .sram persistence, keyboard/joystick DP-5, printer/cassette, Sony speed/pause + Ren-Sha Turbo, SDL3 frontend).
- Impacted Milestones: all future milestones (planner obligation); M14 owns backlog item B9 (VRAM/VDP).
- Risk Notes: The backlog must be kept current every cycle or it silently rots — treat "update backlog" as part of milestone closure. It complements (does not replace) `state/milestones.md`.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-06

- Decision: Open M15 with the north-star GOAL "complete device integrations with the S1985 chipset fully wired" — i.e. replace the M11 chipset SEAMS (PSG #A0-A2, RTC #B4/B5) with real device implementations and complete the remaining device integrations from the deferred backlog. M15 is a PLANNING-ONLY step this cycle: the MSX Planner produces the package, the coordinator STOPS and presents it for human review BEFORE any implementation (honoring the post-planning human-checkpoint rhythm). The planner is directed to consult the ENTIRE deferred-backlog, recommend each item IN vs DEFERRED for M15 with justification, and — because "all pending items" is too large for a single deterministic milestone — PROPOSE a decomposition (M15 as the device-integration milestone + a recommended sequence for the remainder: VDP rendering D1-D7, CPU/VDP cycle timing C1-C4, input/peripherals C6-C8, SDL3 frontend C9), surfacing the scope options for the human to confirm at review. The planner MAY propose add/modify/re-arrange of M1-M14 implementation where required for clean device integration; any such change must be captured in the protocol ledger (decisions/requests/responses/milestones/backlog) per DEC-0005 record-keeping discipline. No production code in this step.
- Impacted Milestones: M15 (new — device-integration / chipset-completion; planning-only this cycle) and, per the planner's proposed decomposition, candidate follow-on milestones for the remaining backlog.
- Risk Notes: Scope is broad and MUST be sliced deterministically; the coordinator will NOT let M15 balloon into an unverifiable mega-milestone — the human review confirms the in/out boundary and the decomposition before implementation. Every deferred-backlog item touched must be status-updated in the same cycle it is addressed. New device fact-sheets (e.g. OPLL/YM2413 for FM-PAC) exist under references/fact-sheets/ and must ground device behavior.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-06

- Decision ID: DEC-0009
- Requested By: Human (project owner) on 2026-07-06 — answers to the M15 planner's scope questions at review.
- Approved By: Human (project owner, source of truth).
- Decision: LOCK the M15 scope per the human's review answers:
  (Q1 boot bar) M15 C5 acceptance = ADVANCE THE A/B BOOT CHECKPOINT past the first PSG/RTC/keyboard reads to a deterministic PC/instruction checkpoint matched to openMSX; M15 does NOT need to reach a BASIC prompt (that needs FDC/cartridge, later).
  (Q2 RTC) RTC uses an IN-MEMORY DETERMINISTIC EPOCH (fixed start each run); file/CMOS persistence deferred to a later persistence milestone — preserves the determinism non-negotiable.
  (Q3 next-after-M15) FDC/DISK IS PRIORITIZED NEXT: the FDC milestone moves up to M16 (ahead of FM-PAC/audio). The remaining follow-on order shifts accordingly and is re-confirmed at each kickoff (indicative: M16 FDC, M17 FM-PAC/OPLL, M18 peripheral I/O, M19 cartridges, M20 Halnote, M21 VDP rendering, M22 sprites/command, M23 exact cycle timing, M24 ZEXALL, M25 Sony speed/pause, M26 SDL3).
  (Q4 audio scope) M15 delivers the NUMERIC/REGISTER-ACCURATE PSG SAMPLE MODEL ONLY (headless, deterministic); actual audio output/presentation is deferred to the SDL3 frontend milestone (C9).
  Coordinator-resolved (not human-gated): Q3-tech (#F5 bit-7 CLOCK-IC gating polarity) and RTC Block-2 boot-config to be grounded by the developer in S1985 fact-sheet §5 + openMSX RP5C01/MSXRTC for A/B parity; Q4-seq (MSX-JE 16KB SRAM, backlog B4) pairs with the FM-PAC/MSX-MUSIC milestone (now M17).
  M15 IN set (final): B1 PSG (numeric), B2 RTC (in-memory epoch), C6 full i8255 PPI + keyboard matrix + joystick, C4 S1985 backup-RAM .sram persistence, C5 boot-checkpoint advance (not BASIC). All other backlog rows remain DEFERRED to the sequence above.
- Impacted Milestones: M15 (scope locked), M16 (now FDC, moved up), and the shifted follow-on sequence.
- Risk Notes: The FDC reorder means audio (FM-PAC) lands after disk; acceptable per human priority (boot/disk progress first). M15 remains headless-deterministic (no audio presentation, no RTC file state). Implementation still HELD pending the human's explicit go-ahead to build (post-planning checkpoint rhythm).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-06

- Decision ID: DEC-0011
- Requested By: Human (project owner) via /msx-master directive "proceed with closing M16 with tagging please."
- Approved By: Human (project owner, source of truth) — release decision.
- Decision: CLOSE M16 (FDC Drive Mechanics — Fujitsu MB89311/WD2793, Sony connection style) on QA PASS (REQ-M16-004 / RESP-M16-004, docs/m16-qa-signoff.md): QA independently reproduced ctest 72/72 (0 failed), zero regression M1-M15 (M9/M12 timing oracles untouched), verified both mid-cycle bug-fix citations (HEAD_LOADED H-flag/idle-timeout semantics; Type-IV i2 index-pulse-scheduled INTRQ) directly against `references/openmsx-21.0/src/fdc/WD2793.cc`, confirmed no test was weakened, and independently diffed the raw openMSX 19.1 A/B trace files (Subject 1: real BIOS-boot empty-diff architectural parity; Subject 2: FDC register/command probe — empty-diff through instruction 37, then a documented/expected cycle-cadence iteration-count difference, converging on an identical terminal register file + byte-identical 512-byte sector transfer). Tag closure snapshot v1.0.16. Closes deferred-backlog row B8 (FDC drive mechanics) -> DONE (M16). C5 (full-boot checkpoint) is honestly left IN-PROGRESS, NOT force-closed: PC-advance signal (d) is satisfied (max PC 0x7D6F, far past M15's 0x488) but the real, unattended BIOS auto-boot handshake (signals (a)-(c): Read Sector accepted / 512 DRQ transfers / clean INTRQ completion) is not observed even after a 20,000,000-instruction diagnostic — accepted as a non-blocking residual per the planner's own pre-declared fallback language and QA's independent judgment, since the FDC device itself is independently proven correct via device-level tests and genuine A/B evidence.
- Impacted Milestones: M16 (closed). Backlog B8 -> DONE (M16); C5 remains IN-PROGRESS with a carried-forward condition: any future milestone claiming C5 fully closed must specifically re-investigate the real MSX auto-disk-boot trigger condition (likely needs disk-ROM/SUB-ROM disassembly or a simulated-keypress investigation) — recorded in `agent-protocol/state/deferred-backlog.md`.
- Risk Notes: Two production bug fixes (HEAD_LOADED semantics, Type-IV i2 scheduling) were made mid-cycle while A/B-probing, outside the original slice plan — both independently verified genuine and correctly grounded by QA, not scope creep. Next milestone (indicative order per DEC-0009: M17 FM-PAC/OPLL + MSX-JE SRAM) not yet kicked off — awaiting a separate human directive to proceed.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-07

- Decision ID: DEC-0012
- Requested By: MSX Planner Agent (`docs/m17-planner-package.md` §2.3/§3.3, REQ-M17-001), flagged as an open question requiring coordinator/human confirmation before implementation.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator) — technical grounding correction, made under the human's standing directive "go ahead and kick off M17 and M18 until QA sign-off... review deferred items and have them properly addressed," which grants the coordinator authority to resolve evidence-grounded scope corrections without pausing the autonomous run, per guardrails Scope Control (incremental, smallest meaningful step) and the Development Accuracy non-negotiable (no fabricated hardware behavior).
- Decision: CORRECT DEC-0009's Q4-seq note ("B4 pairs with the FM-PAC/MSX-MUSIC milestone (now M17)"). Independently re-verified by the coordinator (direct reads of `references/openmsx-21.0/share/machines/Sony_HB-F1XV.xml:105-115,179-197`, `references/openmsx-21.0/src/memory/RomHalnote.cc:37-46`, `references/openmsx-21.0/src/sound/MSXMusic.hh`): the real HB-F1XV's slot-3-3 sound device is openMSX class `MSXMusic` (fixed 16KB ROM + YM2413, I/O-port-only at `#7C/#7D`, **no** `<sramname>` tag, no SRAM, no bank register) — **not** the external `MSXFmPac` cartridge the YM2413 fact-sheet mostly describes. The 16 KB MSX-JE SRAM (backlog B4) is confirmed to belong to the Halnote-mapped MSX-JE firmware ROM at **slot 0-3** (`<sramname>hb-f1xv_msx-je.sram</sramname>`, `<mappertype>Halnote</mappertype>`, `RomHalnote.cc:44` `sram = make_unique<SRAM>(..., 0x4000, ...)` = 16KB) — i.e. backlog row **B6**, not B3. APPROVE the planner's Option A: M17 builds a reusable, standalone, deterministic `BatteryBackedSram` primitive (`src/devices/memory/battery_backed_sram.{h,cpp}`, parametric size, unit-tested at 16KB matching `RomHalnote.cc` exactly, generalizing the M15 S1985 `.sram` load/save discipline) but does **NOT** wire it into slot 3-3 or any other slot this milestone — no real consumer exists until B6/Halnote is implemented, and wiring it into the YM2413 device would fabricate a chip-select overlay this specific machine does not have.
- Impacted Milestones: M17 (B3 closes on the register-accurate YM2413 device only; B4 does NOT close — re-grounded, re-owned to B6, status stays OPEN with the reusable primitive noted as available for reuse). B6/Halnote (indicative M20, unchanged sequencing) is now the confirmed true owner of B4's actual slot wiring. Two new backlog rows approved for tracking: **E1** (YM2413 FM-synthesis DSP/audio depth, mirrors the M14 D1-D7 contract/depth split, paired with C9/SDL3) and **E2** (YM2413 ≥12/84-cycle write-timing constraint, grouped with C1).
- Risk Notes: This corrects a sequencing assumption made without full re-grounding at DEC-0009 time (M15's own planner package had already flagged this ambiguity as an unresolved "Q4" per `docs/m15-planner-package.md`). No hardware behavior is fabricated by this decision — it prevents a fabrication (a nonexistent SRAM overlay in slot 3-3) that the original DEC-0009 phrasing could have led to if followed literally. The reusable primitive still gives real, tested forward progress on B4 without misrepresenting this specific machine's real chip-select map.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-07

- Decision ID: DEC-0013
- Requested By: Human (project owner) via /msx-master directive "close M17 and M18. commit, and tag seperately."
- Approved By: Human (project owner, source of truth) — release decision.

- Decision ID: DEC-0016
- Requested By: Human (project owner) via /msx-master directive "go ahead with M20. ensure that all the backlogs related M20 and up to M20 are all addressed and tested." — the M20 planner's own review (`docs/m20-planner-package.md`, finding A-M20-13) flagged that the already-closed, tagged M17 test suite (v1.0.17) contained a genuine test-harness bug.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator) — a test-only, zero-production-risk correction under DEC-0012's standing precedent (coordinator authority to fix evidence-grounded defects without a human gate when there is no fabrication risk either way).
- Decision: CORRECTED two independently-verified defects in `tests/integration/machine/hbf1xv_m17_ym2413_integration_test.cpp` Case 2 (`FmMusicRom_Slot33Page1_UnchangedByYm2413Writes`, the A-M17-2 regression guard), discovered while reviewing the M20 planner package and confirmed by the coordinator via direct source reading (`src/devices/chipset/slot_bus.cpp`) before any edit was made: (1) **Routing bug** — the test's `#A8`/`#FFFF` setup used `0x0C`, which sets page1's field to primary 3 but leaves page3's field at primary 0; since `SlotBus::write_ffff()` always targets `sub_slot_register_[primary_for_page(3)]` (whichever primary occupies PAGE 3, never the page being logically configured — matching real hardware / openMSX `MSXCPUInterface.cc:757`), the `#FFFF` write silently landed in `sub_slot_register_[0]` instead of `[3]`, so the guard actually read `ram_mapper_` (RAM), not `fmmusic_rom_`. Fixed by using `0xCC` (sets both page1 AND page3 fields to primary 3) for the `#A8` write immediately preceding the `#FFFF` write. (2) **Silent asset-root gap** — this test target never had `SONY_MSX_BIOS_DIR` wired into `tests/CMakeLists.txt` at all (unlike every other test needing real ROM content, e.g. the M15/M16/M18 boot-checkpoint tests), so under `ctest` (whose default working directory is the test binary's own build dir, not the repo root) the default relative `"bios"` asset root resolved to nothing and `fmmusic_rom_`'s image silently 0xFF-filled per the missing-asset policy — meaning even with routing fixed, the guard was checking a degenerate constant window, not real `bios/f1xvmus.rom` content. Fixed by adding the `target_compile_definitions(... SONY_MSX_BIOS_DIR ...)` line and calling `machine.set_asset_root(SONY_MSX_BIOS_DIR)` before `cold_boot()` in Case 2, matching the established pattern. Both fixes were verified: rebuilt, and `ctest --test-dir build -C Debug` now reports 92/92 passed (0 failed), including two new self-documenting assertions (resolved-routing check via `debug_sub_slot_register`/`slot_expanded`, and a non-degenerate-sample sanity check) that make this class of bug fail loudly if it recurs.
- Impacted Milestones: M17 (already closed/tagged v1.0.17) — test-file-only correction, zero production-code change; `git diff` confirms no `src/` file touched. No re-tagging performed (no behavior or shipped-code change); this decision is the disclosure record. M20 unaffected (planning-only at time of this fix).
- Risk Notes: Zero production risk — only `tests/integration/machine/hbf1xv_m17_ym2413_integration_test.cpp` and `tests/CMakeLists.txt` changed. Discovering the second (asset-root) defect was not itself flagged by the M20 planner's A-M20-13 finding (which only identified the routing bug) — the coordinator found it independently while verifying the routing fix actually exercised real ROM content, by running the test binary directly (repo-root cwd, passed) versus via `ctest` (build/tests cwd, failed) and tracing the discrepancy to the missing asset-root wiring. This raises a standing watch-item: any FUTURE test that reads ROM/asset-backed device content and does not call `set_asset_root(SONY_MSX_BIOS_DIR)` will silently run against 0xFF-fill under `ctest`, passing vacuously; developer/QA reviews for M20 and beyond should explicitly check for this pattern whenever a new test asserts real asset-file content.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-07

- Decision ID: DEC-0020
- Requested By: Human (project owner) via /msx-master directive "let's do M21 - M23 ... like we run autopilot until m23" — pre-authorizing the coordinator to proceed through each milestone's release-decision/tag step in this specific three-milestone run without an additional pause request, on a clean QA PASS. This is the THIRD AND FINAL milestone of that run.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), acting on the human's explicit pre-authorization above; QA sign-off (REQ-M23-003/RESP-M23-003, `docs/m23-qa-signoff.md`) reached a clean PASS with no blockers.
- Decision: CLOSE M23 (Exact Cycle Timing — Z80 HALT-R Closure (C2) + VDP Access-Timing Foundation (C1/D4, narrowed)) on QA PASS. This milestone touched the single highest-risk surface in the project (CPU-visible instruction timing, directly adjacent to the M9/M12 CPU-timing-oracle zero-tolerance regression gate) and was deliberately, conservatively scoped: **C2 closes IN FULL** (a small, well-isolated CPU-core fix — `Z80aCpu::step()`'s halted branch now calls the existing `increment_refresh_register()`, keeping the CPU core's own returned T-state count the bare, unchanged datasheet `4`, while the already-existing, unmodified machine-level `datasheet + m1_wait` formula automatically produces the correct 5T MSX-accurate result — grounded byte-for-byte in `references/openmsx-21.0/src/cpu/Z80.hh:19-21` and `CPUCore.cc:2508-2511`, confirmed independently by the coordinator AND QA, both reading the reference source directly). Exactly ONE pre-existing golden test was deliberately updated (`hbf1xv_cpu_step_integration_test.cpp`, t3 4→5, elapsed_cycles 22→23), with the arithmetic independently hand-re-derived by both the coordinator and QA before acceptance; an exhaustive `.halted()` audit (22 pre-existing files) was independently re-run by the planner, the developer, the coordinator, AND QA, confirming zero other test sites needed changing. **C1 and D4 both advance to `IN-PROGRESS (M23 partial)`, deliberately NOT force-closed** — a real, tested, additive, strictly non-gating VDP access-timing foundation ships (`src/devices/video/vdp_access_timing.h`: raster-position derivation, the `VdpAccessDelta` cost-unit enum, two explicitly-separated and never-combined latency facts), while the full ~340-entry per-mode slot tables, the raster-position reconciliation with `run_frame()`'s whole-frame-atomic jump, the CPU-access-steals-command-engine-slot interaction, the command engine's real per-pixel/per-line VDP-cycle cost, the exact sub-frame IRQ raster position, and any actual CPU-execution gating are explicitly named and carried forward as ONE tracked row each (mirrors the D7/C5 "not force-closed, not split into a new letter" precedent). This narrowing was justified by a genuinely new, concrete, DEMONSTRATED risk found during planning: the M21/M22 system-test CPU-program fixtures already contain back-to-back `OUT (#98),A` writes with zero spacer instructions — actually gating CPU execution on VDP-access-wait timing this cycle would risk silently dropping bytes those already-shipped, QA-signed tests depend on, per D4's own documented "too-fast dropped-request" behavior. QA independently confirmed, via its OWN `git diff` against the `v1.0.22` tag, that all 10 named zero-tolerance CPU-timing-oracle test files AND all 6 M21/M22 VDP-device files (`vdp_frame_renderer.{h,cpp}`, `vdp_command_engine.{h,cpp}`, `sprite_engine.{h,cpp}`) show genuinely ZERO changes — the single most important regression-safety confirmation for this milestone, independently reproduced by the coordinator beforehand and by QA again afterward. QA additionally, independently hand-re-derived all 6 new "non-gating proof" fixture T-state totals from the verbatim-copied M21/M22 byte sequences, confirming the new access-timing calculator is genuinely inert. **On the real openMSX A/B evidence for C2** (`docs/m23-parity-trace-diff.md`): the developer honestly reported a DIVERGENCE (R-register mismatches at seq 3-5 of a live WSL openMSX 19.1 session), not a fabricated PASS, with a grounded hypothesis. QA went further still: it independently re-ran the live harness itself (reproducing the identical divergence byte-for-byte), then designed and ran TWO OF ITS OWN exploratory Tcl probes (an exact-reproducibility check, which found the divergence is deterministic rather than real-time-noise-driven, and a boot-window-timing-sensitivity variant, which found the divergence onset tracks emulated time accumulated during the unthrottled pre-measurement boot window) to refine the developer's causal hypothesis from the less-precise "wall-clock time between Tcl round-trips" to the more precise "openMSX's own bulk `advanceHalt` ceiling-division scheduling relative to the boot window's accumulated emulated time" — while confirming, independently, that this is a live-session scheduling artifact and NOT a defect in either engine's R-register logic, since C2's actual closure claim rests on the cited source plus this project's own deterministic tests, not on this live-session probe. **The `src/main.cpp` `--parity-trace halt_idle_extra_steps` CLI extension is hereby formally ratified as an accepted, disclosed, in-scope tooling addition** (ANSWERING QA's Risk 1 recommendation) — an additive, backward-compatible, default-`0`/no-op extension of the existing mode, made necessary by the planner package's own acceptance criterion requiring a genuinely-attempted C2 A/B check (the pre-existing `--parity-trace` mode structurally could not observe halted-idle stepping at all), mirroring the established M19 `--cart1`/`--cart2` precedent of extending the same CLI mode for a new milestone's specific need; independently confirmed safe by both the coordinator and QA via direct diff read (zero touch to any CPU-execution-gating path). Tag closure snapshot v1.0.23. Closes deferred-backlog row **C2** in full; advances **C1** and **D4** to **IN-PROGRESS (M23 partial)**, each with the identical, precisely-named 5-item remainder.
- Impacted Milestones: M23 (closed). Backlog C2 -> DONE (M23); C1, D4 -> IN-PROGRESS (M23 partial), remainder carried forward as one tracked row each. No new backlog rows added this cycle. `src/main.cpp`'s `halt_idle_extra_steps` CLI extension ratified as in-scope (see above). **This decision closes the pre-authorized M21-M23 three-milestone run** in full — the human's 2026-07-07 "let's do M21 - M23 ... like we run autopilot until m23" directive is now fully satisfied: M21 (v1.0.21), M22 (v1.0.22), and M23 (v1.0.23) all closed, tagged, and QA-signed, each with its own dedicated system integration test and independent QA sign-off, per the human's explicit requirements.

A genuine, honestly-disclosed self-caught finding: `PsgYm2149::write_register()` is actually private (the planner's illustrative citation was wrong); the demo mode correctly uses the public `write_address()`/`write_data()` ports instead. Zero changes to any pre-existing file under `src/devices/`, `src/peripherals/`, or `src/core/` (only two genuinely new, additive files, `src/peripherals/msx_key_names.{h,cpp}`); `src/devices/cpu/` and `src/core/` show zero changes of any kind — confirmed via `git diff v1.0.26` at THREE separate gates (developer, coordinator, QA), independently. Zero waveform/DSP-shaped code added for YM2413 anywhere — backlog **E1** stays OPEN, untouched this cycle. Per the human's explicit standing directive this milestone (`feedback_slow_test_cadence.md`), the slow `hbf1xv_m24_zexall_system_test` was NOT run at any gate — the developer, coordinator, and QA each independently confirmed via `git diff v1.0.26 --name-only -- src/devices/ src/peripherals/ src/core/` and `-- src/devices/cpu/ src/core/` that it was genuinely unnecessary, not merely assumed. Headless fast-subset **140/140**; SDL3-ON fast-subset **149/149**; every pre-existing M26 SDL3 test remains green, unmodified. QA independently rebuilt both configurations from clean, reproduced both fast-subset counts exactly, independently launched the real `sony_msx_headless.exe --debug-session` binary itself twice (byte-identical event logs/SHA-256), independently decoded the committed WAV via raw PCM read (not just file-type check), independently confirmed the 71/71 key-name cross-consistency table's completeness via three sources, and independently judged the flat-RAM-driver negative-control design correction genuinely sound via direct PPI-port grounding and hand-derived oracle math. - Decision ID: DEC-0026
- Requested By: Human (project owner), via direct interactive request "in order for me to launch it in full SDL3 mode, where i want to see 'MSX' boot logo, how to do it?" followed by a live black-screen report and explicit direction to investigate ("keep digging now"), then to stop and formalize ("Stop here, write it up") once the second, deeper issue was precisely located (2026-07-08).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), acting under the standing delegation to investigate and fix genuine, human-reported defects directly, mirroring this project's own established practice for developer/coordinator self-caught bugs (M16's HEAD_LOADED divergence, M20's sub-mapper-shadow divergence) — this one discovered via direct human interactive use rather than milestone-internal testing.
- Decision: Land a genuine, well-grounded, tested BUG FIX to the already-shipped M14 `V9958Vdp` device — **not** part of M28's approved scope (E2/C5/health-audit) and **not** touching backlog C1/D4's own license-sensitive remainder. Full finding and fix documented in `docs/vdp-vr-hr-boot-hang-fix-report.md`. Summary: a real, CPU-driven interactive boot of the actual Sony BIOS through the SDL3 frontend produced a **permanent black screen** — root-caused via direct instruction-level investigation to `V9958Vdp::peek_status_register(2)` hardcoding status bits VR (bit6, "vblank area") and HR (bit5, "hblank area") to a fixed 0, a disclosed M23 simplification tied to backlog C1/D4. The real BIOS polls VR in a wait-for-toggle loop during its very first VDP-initialization step, before writing a single VDP register — since VR never toggled, the BIOS hung forever and never configured the VDP, hence the black screen. Confirmed via a targeted hypothesis test (forcing VR to a constant 1 reproduces the identical hang on the opposite edge, proving genuine toggling is required, not a specific fixed value). **Fix**: a new, optional, attach-only `VdpClockSource` (X-pattern of the already-established `RtcClockSource`/`FdcClockSource`/`CassetteClockSource`/`RenshaTurboClockSource`/`Ym2413ClockSource` adapters), supplying `cpu_tstates_since_vsync()` from the machine's own pre-existing `cycles_since_last_vsync()` formula (unchanged since M23); VR/HR now computed LIVE from real elapsed raster position when a clock source is attached (nullptr by default, zero behavior change otherwise), grounded directly in `references/fact-sheets/Yamaha V9958 VDP.md` §7's own NTSC line/frame timing tables and reusing M23's own already-shipped, non-gating `vdp_access_timing::vdp_cycle_within_line()` foundation — **zero license-sensitive data involved**, the ~340-entry per-slot access-timing tables that are C1/D4's actual real remainder are completely untouched. Consulted PULL-STYLE only from `peek_status_register(2)`, never wired into `step_cpu_instruction()`/`run_cycles()`/`run_frame()` (confirmed: zero touch to `src/devices/cpu/` or `src/core/`). **Empirically verified**: the previously-permanent black screen now correctly configures the VDP (R#0-R#8 non-zero) and shows the correct MSX blue background color within ~300 frames (a real, directly-viewed screenshot, `debug/frames/diag-fixed-300.png`). New dedicated unit test (`tests/unit/devices/video_vdp_vr_hr_raster_status_unit_test.cpp`, 9 cases) and integration test (`tests/integration/machine/hbf1xv_vdp_vr_hr_raster_integration_test.cpp`, 4 cases) added. **A genuine regression was found and fixed same-cycle**: `tests/integration/machine/hbf1xv_m24_cpm_run_integration_test.cpp`'s device-isolation invariant failed on first full-suite run, because that test's "before vs after 10,000 real CPU instructions" VDP-state snapshot comparison now legitimately differs on VR/HR specifically (time genuinely passes during that test's own CPU-only exerciser, which never calls `on_vsync_boundary()`) — correctly identified as expected, intended new behavior (not a cross-device-state-leakage violation, independently re-verified via every OTHER register/status-bit/palette-entry/all 131,072 VRAM bytes in the same snapshot remaining an exact, unmasked match) and fixed by masking VR/HR (bits `0x60`) specifically out of that ONE test's S#2 comparison, with the reasoning recorded inline. Full regression: `ctest -LE m24_slow_full_sweep` **145/145 passed** (fast subset); per the standing `feedback_slow_test_cadence.md` mechanical gate (an existing `src/devices/` file was touched), the full unfiltered `ctest` including the slow ZEXALL/ZEXDOC sweep was re-run to completion (`build/full_sweep_vrhr.log`). **A second, deeper finding was precisely located but NOT fixed this cycle, per the human's explicit direction to stop and formalize**: a real openMSX 19.1 A/B instruction-trace comparison (1,268,860 instructions, the established M10-M28 parity technique) found the exact FIRST divergence at instruction #145,503, `PC=0x0455` (inside the BIOS's RAM-mapper segment/size self-test loop) — a single-byte content mismatch (`0xFF` vs `0x00`) at logical address `0x8001` (memory-mapper segment 1, physical RAM offset `0x4001`), with every architectural field (PC, all registers, flags, IFF1/IFF2/IM) matching openMSX exactly up to and including that instruction. This is fully documented in `docs/vdp-vr-hr-boot-hang-fix-report.md` §4 as an open, precisely-located finding for a future cycle — NOT related to C1/D4 or any license-sensitive data, likely a memory-mapper segment-register write-history question requiring its own dedicated trace-back investigation, comparable in shape to C5's own auto-boot-trigger work.
- Impacted Milestones: none directly (a standalone bug fix, landed between M28's developer-implementation-complete state and its QA dispatch — M28's own approved scope, E2/C5/health-audit, is unaffected and unchanged by this fix). Backlog **C1/D4** gains a factual, non-status-changing cross-reference note: its own prior "HR/VR remain idle 0" disclosure is now superseded by this fix (VR/HR are live), but the row's actual remainder (the license-sensitive ~340-entry access-slot timing tables) is completely unaffected, unchanged, and still ruled UNBUILDABLE-WITHOUT-FABRICATION per DEC-0025/`docs/m28-planner-package.md` §2.2. No new backlog row opened this cycle for the §4 finding (memory-mapper segment-history divergence) — documented in `docs/vdp-vr-hr-boot-hang-fix-report.md` §4 for a future cycle to pick up and formally register, per the human's explicit direction to stop investigating further for now.
- Risk Notes: (1) This fix changes OBSERVABLE VDP behavior (S#2 bits 5/6 are no longer a fixed constant) — any future test or tool that assumes a frozen/constant S#2 value across a time-advancing operation must account for this, exactly as the M24 CP/M-isolation test needed to; this risk is now documented inline in that test and in this fix's own report. (2) The §4 finding (memory-mapper segment-content divergence) is a genuine, reproducible, precisely-located defect somewhere in this project's boot-time behavior (or, less likely, a real difference in openMSX's own default RAM initialization) — left OPEN, honestly disclosed, not force-investigated further this cycle per explicit human direction. (3) The temporary diagnostic scaffolding used to investigate both findings (a `--boot-frame-dump` CLI mode, ad hoc byte-peek instrumentation) was deliberately NOT committed — `src/main.cpp` was reverted to its pre-investigation state; only the VERIFIED fix (v9958_vdp.*, machine wiring) and its PROPER tests are landed.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-08

- Decision ID: DEC-0028
- Requested By: Human (project owner), choosing "memory-mapper divergence" as the next work item after M28's closure (2026-07-08).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), acting under the DEC-0026 precedent for targeted, coordinator-authorized bug investigations outside the milestone process.
- Decision: CLOSE the instruction-#145,503 memory-mapper/RAM-content divergence investigation with a **"no bug found — original finding was a false positive"** outcome, fully documented in `docs/memory-mapper-segment-divergence-investigation.md`. The developer agent first independently reproduced both sides' state at the exact divergence point and **disconfirmed the segment-register hypothesis** (page 2's mapper segment is `1` on BOTH emulators — the full page→segment map `3,2,1,0` matches openMSX's own documented MSX2+ BIOS convention identically). Digging further found the actual root cause: **the originally-reported "openMSX reads 0x00 where this emulator reads 0xFF" claim (DEC-0026's §4 finding) was an artifact of the ad-hoc live-Tcl comparison technique, not a defect in this project's code.** The established M10-M28 harness pattern lets openMSX free-run several real seconds under its own autoboot before issuing a Tcl `reset` — and real MSX hardware's reset (faithfully modeled by openMSX, grounded in `MSXMemoryMapperBase.cc:41-52`: `powerUp()` clears RAM, `reset()` only zeroes mapper registers) does NOT clear RAM. The free-run had already legitimately written `0x00` to that physical byte; the bare `reset` silently preserved it into the comparison state. This was safe for every prior M10-M28 A/B check (all CPU-register-only — `trace-diff.py` has no memory-content field) but NOT for the one-off memory-content check that produced the §4 finding. Proven four independent, converging ways: (1) inserting a genuine power-cycle (`set power off/on`) makes openMSX read `0xFF` — exact match with this emulator; (2) the "divergent" value flips 0x00/0xFF purely as a function of unrelated free-run duration (0.1s clean, 2s/6s contaminated) — definitionally contamination, not a deterministic property; (3) openMSX watchpoints vs. this emulator's own write log show byte-identical write histories (same two instructions #145,505/#145,508, same FF→00→FF transitions — the BIOS's own non-destructive RAM probe) over a 300,000-instruction window under the corrected comparison; (4) this project's `initialize_dram_pattern()` was independently verified byte-exact against the machine XML's own initialContent formula. **Zero production code changed** (`git diff v1.0.28 -- src/` empty; the temporary diagnostic was fully reverted); fast-subset ctest 145/145, unchanged baseline; slow sweep mechanically not required (zero src/devices|peripherals|core touch). `docs/vdp-vr-hr-boot-hang-fix-report.md` §4 received a clearly-labeled correction addendum (original text preserved, mirroring the established stale-figure-caveat precedent). A genuine methodology lesson is recorded for all future memory-content A/B work: **RAM-content comparisons against live openMSX REQUIRE a genuine power-cycle (`set power off/on`), never a bare Tcl `reset`** — plus a documented off-by-one in the `after break`/`step` instruction-count-targeting idiom.
- Impacted Milestones: none (investigation-only, zero code change). DEC-0026's §4 secondary finding is SUPERSEDED (the primary VR/HR fix and all its tests/evidence are entirely unaffected — QA independently reproduced that fix separately, and its correctness never depended on the §4 finding). The memory-mapper/RAM subsystem (`memory_mapper_ram.cpp`, `mapper_io.cpp`, DRAM initial-content pattern) is now POSITIVELY confirmed correct — byte-identical physical write history vs. real openMSX over a 300,000-instruction corrected-methodology window, a stronger clean bill of health than it had before the false positive arose. One genuinely open remainder, honestly carried forward (see `docs/memory-mapper-segment-divergence-investigation.md` §5): the separate "~2.8-2.9M instruction downstream dead-end" observation (repeating RST 38 stack corruption → permanent HALT) was originally framed as downstream of the now-refuted content mismatch, so its actual cause — and whether it is a real divergence from openMSX at all — is now an open question; NOT investigated this cycle (out of the assigned scope), a candidate for a future dedicated check using the corrected power-cycle methodology.
- Risk Notes: (1) The corrected-methodology requirement (power-cycle, not reset, for any memory-content A/B) is recorded in the investigation report §3 and this entry — future investigations MUST use it or will reproduce the same class of false positive. (2) The downstream-dead-end open item is the natural next candidate if the human wants to continue the boot-completion thread; it should be A/B-checked from scratch with the corrected methodology rather than trusting the original single-sided observation. (3) No new backlog row opened (consistent with how the §4 finding itself was handled — tracked via docs + decision entries, pending an explicit future directive).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-08

- Decision ID: DEC-0029
- Requested By: Human (project owner), via live interactive playtesting: Metal Gear ran (backgrounds/sound/input all working) but the player sprite — and all sprites — were completely invisible; the human explicitly directed the fix be at the UNIVERSAL hardware level, never a game-specific patch (now a standing project memory, `feedback_universal_fixes_only.md`) (2026-07-08).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), on QA's clean, unconditional PASS (`docs/sprite-fix-qa-review.md`), per the standing continuation cadence and the DEC-0026/DEC-0028 targeted-fix precedent.
- Decision: LAND the sprite-mode-2 attribute-table addressing fix (`src/devices/video/sprite_engine.cpp`), fully documented in `docs/sprite-invisibility-investigation.md`. **Root cause (universal, not game-specific):** in sprite mode 2, the V9958's sprite attribute-table registers form an AND-MASK, not a plain base address — effective address = `((R#11<<15)|(R#5<<7)|0x7F) & (~0x3FF | index)`, grounded in `references/openmsx-21.0/src/video/VDP.cc:1357-1371` (`updateSpriteAttributeBase`), `VDPVRAM.hh:263-279`, `SpriteChecker.cc:283-330`. R#5's low 3 bits are mask bits real software universally sets to 1 (BIOS SCREEN5 `R#5=0xEF`, Metal Gear `R#5=0xE7`); the pre-fix M22 `SpriteEngine` treated R#5 as a plain base and added +512, landing every mode-2 Y/X/pattern read 0x200 bytes too high (zeros) — every sprite in every MSX2 sprite-mode-2 title invisible. This also retroactively explains M22's own recorded `sprite_mode2_ninth_ic` A/B divergence. New regression test (`tests/unit/devices/video_sprite_engine_mode2_attribute_masking_unit_test.cpp`: exact Metal Gear register shape end-to-end to FrameBuffer pixels, a decoy planted at the pre-fix address, determinism); two existing tests corrected from bug-compatible `R#5=0x00` programming to the real-software mask-bit convention (QA-judged legitimate corrections, zero assertions weakened). **QA (`docs/sprite-fix-qa-review.md`): clean PASS, zero Critical/High/Medium findings**, with exceptional verification depth: (1) the planar G6/G7 equivalence question (openMSX transforms masks into planar space; our fix masks in logical space then rotates) PROVEN equivalent for ALL register values via bit-permutation distributivity over AND/OR — not just the mask-bits-set convention; (2) the new test confirmed to FAIL on a real v1.0.28 pre-fix worktree build with exactly the predicted 5 failures (discriminating, both directions); (3) QA's own independent public-API-only harness reproduced BOTH evidence PNGs SHA256-identical to the developer's (before `1e7dc436...`, after `e67845b1...`) — a byte-exact, cross-harness evidence chain; (4) zero game-specific logic confirmed (the universal-fix directive honored); (5) zero touch to `src/devices/cpu/`/`src/core/`. Regression: developer's full unfiltered suite 147/147 including the ZEXALL/ZEXDOC sweep (`error_markers=0` both suites, coordinator-confirmed from the raw log at the time); QA clean-rebuild fast subset 146/146. Empirical headline: `debug/frames/mg-sprite-invisibility-{before,after}.png` + openMSX reference — the player sprite is now visible at the same position openMSX renders it.
- Impacted Milestones: none directly (targeted fix). M22's sprite CONTRACT is corrected; M22's `docs/m22-parity-trace-diff.md` `sprite_mode2_ninth_ic` divergence is retroactively explained (probe pins `R#5=0x00`, bug-compatible aliasing programming — re-baselining that probe, `tools/gen-m22-sprite-cmd-probe.py:157`, stays a deferred follow-up per `docs/sprite-invisibility-investigation.md` §6.3). **Two standing process changes ratified in this same cycle (human-approved):** (1) `feedback_universal_fixes_only.md` — all fixes at the universal hardware level, never game-keyed; (2) `feedback_slow_test_cadence.md` REFINED — the slow ZEXALL/ZEXDOC sweep is required only for CPU-visible timing-path changes (cpu/core/instruction-stepping/bus-slot-mapper-IO dispatch); pure pull-model renderer/frontend components are exempt; when required it runs ONCE (developer), reviewers verify the captured log (QA's in-flight redundant re-run was deliberately stopped mid-sweep by the coordinator per the human's explicit direction — the aborted `build-qa2` full run is intentional, not a failure).
- Risk Notes: (1) QA finding F3 (Low): the developer's 147/147 full-sweep log was later overwritten in `build/Testing/Temporary/LastTest.log` by a subsequent fast run — the sweep result is attested by the developer's report + the coordinator's contemporaneous read of the raw log, but is no longer independently verifiable on disk; future required sweeps should copy the log to a durable path (non-gating here since the refined cadence rule exempts this component anyway). (2) The M22 probe re-baseline (`R#5=0x00` pin) remains deferred. (3) Remaining open user-reported presentation items queued next: missing MSX2+ boot-logo animation, missing border/backdrop region in the SDL3 presenter, SDL3 audio latency (recorded, not investigated).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-08

- Decision ID: DEC-0030
- Requested By: Human (project owner): "note that i added source codes and executable and roms to references/fmsx-60/ for your cross reference for your implementation. this is completely freeware but again i want you to use it for your reference to tighten our work. review it and make sure this is fully propagated across agents and projects." (2026-07-08).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), mirroring the DEC-0021 (`disks/`) asset-propagation precedent.
- Decision: REGISTER `references/fmsx-60/` (fMSX 6.0 by Marat Fayzullin: `source/` with fMSX/EMULib/Z80 modules, `executables/` with fMSX.exe + generic MSX ROMs + CARTS.SHA, ~1.8 MB) as an **independent second behavior cross-reference**, propagated across all governance surfaces: `CLAUDE.md` (Reference materials + Repository layout), `agent-protocol/project-baseline.md` (Reference Materials + Repository Directories + directory usage rules), `agent-protocol/guardrails.md` (grounding-preference + never-copy rules), and the msx-planner/msx-developer/msx-qa agent definitions. **License verified by direct read** (source headers: "Copyright (C) Marat Fayzullin... You are not allowed to distribute this software commercially"): freeware, non-commercial distribution only, NOT open-source — the SAME hard isolation rule as openMSX applies (read for understanding, never copy code into `src/`), and its large data tables fall under the standing zero-license-sensitive-work directive (`feedback_license_sensitive_scope.md`) exactly like openMSX's. **Value**: an implementation lineage independent of openMSX — a second, independent opinion for triangulating device behavior (V9938 command engine `source/fMSX/V9938.c`, AY8910 PSG / YM2413 / SCC / WD1793-family FDC / i8255 PPI under `source/EMULib/`, a Z80 core under `source/Z80/`, plus `CARTS.SHA`, a cartridge-identification SHA database relevant to backlog G2 if ever scheduled). A new cross-reference discipline is codified in the governance files: when the two behavior references disagree, record the disagreement explicitly and prefer the fact-sheet/real-hardware-corroborated interpretation — never silently pick one. The bundled generic MSX ROMs (`executables/*.ROM`) are cross-reference assets only (this machine uses the Sony-specific `bios/` set); same non-redistribution discipline as `bios/`/`roms/`/`disks/`.
- Impacted Milestones: none retroactively; all future investigations/milestones gain the second reference. Notably relevant to already-named future work: M29 (KonamiSCC — fMSX has an independent `SCC.c`), M30 (YM2413 DSP — independent `YM2413.c`), M31 (FDC flux — independent `WD1793.c`/`FDIDisk.c`), G2 (`CARTS.SHA`).
- Risk Notes: (1) fMSX is a behavior reference of a different accuracy tier than openMSX (fMSX historically favors portability/simplicity over cycle exactness) — disagreements between the two are expected and are signals for fact-sheet arbitration, not automatic errors in either. (2) The never-copy rule is, if anything, STRICTER than openMSX's GPL case (no license grant at all beyond personal use) — zero code or table transcription under any framing. (3) `references/fmsx-60/` is a local development asset; do not assert redistribution rights (same as `bios/`/`roms/`/`disks/`).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-08

- Decision ID: DEC-0031
- Requested By: Human (project owner), via live interactive playtesting: (A) the BASIC screen lacked the surrounding sky-blue border box a real MSX displays ("it's blue-sky border surrounding the msx-blue inside... just missing surrounding box"); (B) the MSX2+ boot-logo animation never appeared at boot (human supplied a reference screenshot of the expected logo screen) (2026-07-08).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), on QA's clean PASS (`docs/border-boot-logo-qa-review.md`), per the standing continuation cadence and the DEC-0026/DEC-0029 targeted-fix precedent.
- Decision: LAND both presentation fixes, fully documented in `docs/border-and-boot-logo-investigation.md`. **(A) Border/backdrop composition**: the renderer computed a mode-aware R#7 border color every frame but `Sdl3VideoPresenter` blitted only the bare active area, full-window — the border region was never presented. New `src/frontend/border_composer.{h,cpp}` (pure, SDL-free composition: active area at its raster-true anchor inside a live border-colored 320x240/640x240 canvas; anchors 32/41/64/82 × 24/14 derived from the V9958 fact-sheet §7 tick tables + openMSX `SDLRasterizer.cc` and verified against measured openMSX Sony_HB-F1XV screenshots); presenter composes before upload; `tools/frame-to-png.py` gains `--with-border`. **(B) Boot logo — THREE stacked root causes plus one latent crash, fixed in causal order**: (1) port #F4 reset-status register was entirely missing — open-bus 0xFF reads made the BIOS take the warm-restart path and skip the logo routine; new `src/devices/chipset/reset_status_register.{h,cpp}` (non-inverted per `Sony_HB-F1XV.xml:80-83`, semantics per `MSXResetStatusRegister.cc:13-35`; QA independently hex-dumped `bios/f1xvbios.rom` and confirmed the `IN/OUT (0F4h)` accesses at 0x146A/0x146F); the RTC-CMOS hypothesis was investigated and ruled out (our post-boot CMOS block 2 is byte-identical to openMSX's). (2) the S#0 sprite-collision flag was frame-granular — the SUB-ROM logo wobble loop polls it per line and ran ~200x slow; `sprite_engine`/`v9958_vdp` now maintain per-line collision events re-latched against the live raster position on S#0 reads (pull-style clock, clockless-safe no-op). **A genuine openMSX-vs-fMSX reference DISAGREEMENT was recorded and arbitrated per DEC-0030's discipline**: fMSX checks collisions once per frame (`MSX.c:2178-2184`, the exact pre-fix model); the real BIOS's own polling protocol (84 poll-exits inside a measured ~0.5-0.75s wobble window — impossible at one exit/frame) proves line granularity is the hardware behavior; QA independently verified the arbitration arithmetic. (3) the VDP command engine never honored a pre-armed COL transfer unit — the BIOS pre-loads LMMC pixel 0 into R#44 before starting the command, then sends NX*NY-1 more; both references AGREE here (openMSX `VDPCmdEngine.cc:1856-1863` + fMSX `V9938.c:852-857` — the new second reference corroborating on its first day in the repo); `vdp_command_engine` now arms `transfer_pending_` on any R#44 write and consumes it as the first unit. (4) latent OOB write fixed: GRAPHIC5/6 sprite compositing clipped at canvas width (512) instead of sprite-space 256. **Post-fix boot matches openMSX phase-for-phase**: logo entry frame 75, exit 259 (QA-corrected from the report's original 270 transcription error), BASIC at ~4.3s vs openMSX ~4.5s, final #F4=0x80, BASIC-time registers byte-identical; the Sony BIOS renders its authentic "Main RAM:64Kbytes" variant (64KB correct per the Target Machine Specification; the human's reference screenshot was the generic MSX2P.ROM two-line variant, an expected BIOS difference, documented). Tests: 5 new unit + 1 new integration (`machine_hbf1xv_boot_logo_integration_test`, real-BIOS end-to-end logo timeline) + 2 legitimate test corrections (presenter pixel test for composed geometry; the M22 system test updated to the authentic COL pre-load protocol — its old ordering encoded the reference-divergent pre-fix contract, mirroring DEC-0029's R#5 precedent). Headless fast subset **152/152**; SDL3-ON fast subset **161/161** (independently reproduced by QA from a fresh build). ZEXALL sweep correctly NOT run per the RC-checkpoint cadence (third revision, ratified this same day) — zero `src/devices/cpu/`/`src/core/` touch. QA adversarially verified all three headline fixes genuinely fail on pre-fix code (worktree build: pending-COL 8 failures, collision-relatch fails, boot-logo integration fails with `entry=-1 exit=-1 f4_end=0xff` — the human-reported defect verbatim). All 9 evidence PNGs committed under `debug/frames/` (gitignore-excepted).
- Impacted Milestones: none directly (targeted fixes). M14/M22's VDP contract gains the #F4 chipset sibling, line-granular collision, and the pre-armed COL protocol; M26's presenter gains border composition. QA findings (all Low/Info, applied at commit time): stale exit=270 doc figure corrected to 259; the boot-logo-before PNG is byte-identical to the border-after PNG (both are the same static blank frame — content-consistent, noted for hygiene; the pre-fix claims rest on the adversarial worktree runs, not that PNG); unrelated working-tree items (`.claude/settings.json`, `disks/games/`, `build-qa*`) kept out of this commit.
- Risk Notes: (1) The wobble scroll positions were not pixel-diffed frame-by-frame against openMSX (phase timeline + end-state register identity only) — a future refinement candidate, not a defect. (2) GRAPHIC5's dual border colors remain the documented even-half simplification. (3) Without a mounted disk, BASIC appears only after a >40s drive-detect phase — pre-existing behavior (per M16/M28 artifacts), NOT a regression from this cycle. (4) The frame-granular fMSX collision model is now a KNOWN reference limitation — future collision work should weight openMSX + the BIOS-protocol evidence accordingly.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-08

- Decision ID: DEC-0032
- Requested By: Human (project owner), via live playtesting: Metal Gear's Konami splash rendered on a BLACK background (expected WHITE, believed a DEC-0031 regression); the human also decided against the DEC-0031 border presentation after seeing it live ("it is okay to remove this skyblue border i asked.. not needed") (2026-07-08).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), on QA's clean, unconditional PASS (`docs/konami-splash-qa-review.md`), per the standing continuation cadence and the DEC-0026/DEC-0029/DEC-0031 precedent.
- Decision: LAND both changes, fully documented in `docs/konami-splash-regression-investigation.md`. **(1) The suspected regression was proven EMPIRICALLY NOT A REGRESSION**: per-frame hash forensics between HEAD (6f89552) and a 289a40f worktree showed all 215 sampled splash frames hash-identical and the settled splash dumps byte-identical (sha256 `711dd97a...` both sides) — DEC-0031 changed nothing about this content (its white border simply made the always-black content conspicuous), and QA additionally proved the new regression test fails with the IDENTICAL 5 cases at BOTH prior commits. The DEC-0031 pre-armed-COL suspect was formally EXONERATED via a complete transfer-flag-lifecycle audit of both references (openMSX `VDPCmdEngine.cc` set/clear/consume sites; fMSX `V9938.c`) — our engine matches both. **The real defect was pre-existing and universal: missing V99x8 color-0 transparency** — when R#8 TP is CLEAR (the default), color index 0 in screen CONTENT displays the backdrop color (R#7 low nibble), not raw palette entry 0; Metal Gear's splash leaves its background at color 0 with backdrop=white, which our renderer had always shown as palette-0 black. Fixed universally in `src/devices/video/vdp_frame_renderer.{h,cpp}` (`content_pal16()`/`content_pal16_g5()` applied at exactly the reference's content call sites: TEXT1/TEXT2-plain/G1/G2/G3/MC/G4/G5-split/G6/YAE-palette-branch; sprites, border, GRAPHIC7, TEXT2-blink, and pure-YJK deliberately excluded, matching openMSX `SDLRasterizer.cc:346-373`/`VDP.hh:189-191`). **A genuine openMSX-vs-fMSX reference DISAGREEMENT recorded and arbitrated per DEC-0030**: fMSX applies the substitution unconditionally (`Common.h:76`, no TP modeling); openMSX conditions it on TP; the V9938 data-book model (TP=1 = opaque opt-out over the TMS9918-lineage transparent default) supports openMSX — QA independently verified the polarity direction (the classic trap) against both sources. A "R#0 TP" register-number typo found in the fact-sheet by QA (F3) was corrected in place (TP is R#8 bit5). **(2) Border presentation now OPT-IN**: the default presents the bare active area (byte-exact pre-DEC-0031 behavior, proven by the rewritten pixel integration test); a new `--border` CLI flag enables the untouched, still-tested `border_composer` path — the hardware-grounded capability is preserved, the human's preferred default restored. Tests: NEW `video_vdp_frame_renderer_color0_backdrop_unit_test` (verified failing pre-fix with exactly 5 cases, by developer AND QA independently); pending-COL unit test extended with the stale-arm lifecycle case; `--border` parse coverage; presenter pixel test proves BOTH paths. Headless fast subset **153/153**; SDL3-ON **162/162** (both independently re-run by QA). Boot-logo integration UNCHANGED (`entry=75 exit=259 f4_end=0x80`; post-fix logo frame pixel-identical to DEC-0031's committed evidence, PIL diff bbox=None). BASIC-screen impact empirically confirmed nil (TEXT/BASIC uses non-zero R#7 nibbles — identity there). Evidence PNGs committed under `debug/frames/` (before-black/after-white/openMSX-reference/post-colorfix-logo). QA finding F1 applied at commit time (the incidentally-regenerated `docs/openmsx-ab-smoke.md` was restored, preserving its historical R5-resolution note).
- Impacted Milestones: none directly (targeted fix). M21's renderer gains the color-0/backdrop hardware behavior it had always lacked — a Target-Spec accuracy improvement discovered only through live human playtesting (the third such find this session). The DEC-0031 border capability remains shipped but default-off.
- Risk Notes: (1) Color-0 content across ALL palette modes now legitimately shows backdrop where it previously showed palette-0 black — intended, data-book-correct behavior; any future test/tool asserting the old raw-palette-0 pixels must update (none existed). (2) fMSX's unconditional model is now a second KNOWN fMSX limitation (after frame-granular collision, DEC-0031) — future arbitrations should weight accordingly. (3) The human's "was white before" recollection is honestly documented as not reproducible (§8 of the investigation doc) — most plausibly a perception artifact of the border change; no evidence of any transient white-rendering state was found.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-08

- Decision ID: DEC-0033
- Requested By: Human (project owner), via live playtesting: PSG sound effects arriving 0.5-1 second late (e.g. Metal Gear's punch on the N key), with explicit direction to fix it as the final item before closing the playtesting-hardening arc (2026-07-08).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), on QA's clean, unconditional PASS (`docs/audio-latency-qa-review.md`), per the standing continuation cadence and the DEC-0026..DEC-0032 precedent.
- Decision: LAND the audio-pacing fix, fully documented in `docs/audio-latency-investigation.md`. **Measured root cause (three compounding parts)**: (1) `run_interactive()` truncated the exact 16,688,154.5 ns frame period to a flat 16 ms `SDL_Delay` target — the emulator measurably ran at **61.61 fps instead of the authentic 59.9227 Hz (~3% fast)**, overproducing +1,244 audio samples/s; (2) `run_one_frame()` pushed `floor(59736/81)=737` samples/frame vs the exact 735.948 (+65/s more); (3) `SDL_PutAudioStreamData` queues unboundedly with zero backpressure, so every excess sample became permanent latency — measured pre-fix: **+29.7 ms of lag per second of play** (the human's 0.5-1 s report is reached in 17-34 s and would keep growing without bound). **Fix (frontend-only; zero device/machine/core changes)**: new SDL-free `src/frontend/audio_pacer.{h,cpp}` — exact cumulative accounting `total_due = floor(elapsed_cycles*44100/3579545)` via an overflow-safe `scale_cycles` (headroom ~585 emulated years), 67 ms hard queue cap with trim-to-reconverge, 33 ms low-water silence re-prime only at genuine underrun; `Sdl3AudioPresenter::pump_and_push_paced()` always advances the PSG pump by the FULL exact delta (generator time never desyncs from machine time — trimming drops only pushed PCM, a determinism-critical property QA verified in code and tests); `run_interactive()` now uses exact-ns absolute deadlines (`SDL_GetTicksNS`/`SDL_DelayNS`, cumulative-cycle-derived so error stays <1 ns forever) with 100 ms stall forgiveness. Pacing policy grounded in openMSX's bounded ~69.7 ms driver ring (`SDLSoundDriver.cc` — QA refined the citation: the drop branch is openMSX's unthrottled fallback, the right analogue since our frame loop is the throttle) and independently corroborated by fMSX's latency-bounded ring (`EMULib/Unix/SndUnix.c:180`). **Determinism preserved**: the only emulated-state-touching output (`samples_to_pump`) is a pure function of cycle counts; host queue state gates only what is pushed to SDL. **Post-fix, measured twice independently** (developer, then QA with its own probe on its own build): frame rate 59.9229/59.9226 fps; queue bounded 30.4-50.9/25.8-49.4 ms (mean 41.1/37.6 ms) over ~3-minute real-WASAPI Metal Gear sessions; residual +3.3/+3.85 samples/s clock-domain skew absorbed by the cap by design. **Side benefit**: the entire emulator now runs at the exact authentic MSX speed (it had been ~3% fast since M26). Tests: new `frontend_audio_pacer_unit_test` (4-hour no-drift proof against an independent oracle, 735/736-only deltas, exact-ns period, overflow safety, cap/trim/stall-reconvergence — QA adversarially confirmed the old 737-arithmetic fails them immediately); extended presenter integration test (also passes on the REAL WASAPI driver, not just dummy). Headless fast subset **154/154**; SDL3-ON **163/163** (both independently reproduced by QA). ZEXALL correctly not run (frontend-only, RC-checkpoint cadence).
- Impacted Milestones: none directly (targeted fix). M26's frontend gains correct real-time pacing and bounded audio latency; the disclosed 81-cycle PSG generator step (−3.6 cent constant pitch offset) is retained and now explicitly documented. This completes the last open defect report of the 2026-07-08 live-playtesting arc (DEC-0028..DEC-0033); arc closure (C5 ledger reconciliation + checkpoint tag v1.0.29) is gated on the human's own audible confirmation, per their explicit instruction.
- Risk Notes: (1) Long sessions settle near the 67 ms cap with periodic few-sample trims (bounded by design, comparable to openMSX's own ring) — the human's long-session listen is the final acceptance check. (2) `SDL_GetAudioStreamQueued` error (-1) is treated as empty queue → a one-shot ≤33 ms silence re-prime on SDL error only; benign, QA-noted. (3) Game feel is now authentically ~3% slower than the (incorrectly fast) pre-fix behavior — intended, correct, disclosed to the human.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-08

- Decision ID: DEC-0034
- Requested By: Human (project owner): "verify+close C5 backlog row, ledger reconciliation, tag v1.0.29, and yes to register disks/games/" — the closure of the 2026-07-08 live-playtesting hardening arc, after the human's acceptance of the DEC-0033 audio fix (2026-07-09).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), executing the human's explicit closure directive.
- Decision: **CLOSE the live-playtesting hardening arc (DEC-0028..DEC-0034) and tag `v1.0.29`.** Three components:

  **(1) Backlog C5 ("full boot past first device read") — VERIFIED and CLOSED, DONE (DEC-0034), after 12 milestones open (M13→now).** The auto-disk-boot "trigger mystery" is answered: there was never a missing trigger — the boot could not reach the disk phase because of three since-fixed defects (DEC-0026's VR/HR status-poll hang; DEC-0031's missing #F4 reset-status register sending the BIOS down the warm-restart path, plus its collision-granularity and COL-transfer fixes), and the prior negative diagnostics (M16, M28) additionally ran step-only loops without `on_vsync_boundary()` — no VBlank interrupts, so the boot stalls by construction under that loop shape (the M28 C5 system test's negative result is retained, documented as exactly that loop-shape artifact). **Closure evidence, deterministic and coordinator-run**: an unattended (zero-input) real frame-loop cold boot with the real `disks/msxdos22.dsk` mounted — disk-ROM window paged into page 1 at frame 300; `read_sector_commands_accepted=11` / `read_sector_completions_ok=11` (the DSKCHG→Restore→Read-Sector handshake executing for real); settled at the full MSX-BASIC prompt with `Disk BASIC version 1.0` loaded (`debug/frames/c5-verify-settled.png`, committed — matching the human's own live screenshot). Honest residual (non-blocking per the row's own "full boot to a prompt" bar, recorded in the row): the unattended MSX-DOS-2.2-disk boot lands at the Disk BASIC prompt rather than the MSX-DOS `A>` shell — whether MSXDOS.SYS should fully take over on this configuration is a narrower future fidelity question; the disk-ROM boot handshake itself is proven working.

  **(2) `disks/games/` registered** (human-provided; currently the two-disk YS II set) across `CLAUDE.md` and the msx-developer agent definition — same legally-sourced, non-redistributable local-dev-asset discipline as `bios/`/`roms/`/`disks/`; purpose: live/regression playtesting of the disk-boot and (future) multi-disk paths.

  **(3) Tag `v1.0.29` — "live-playtesting hardening."** The arc's ledger: DEC-0028 (memory-mapper divergence resolved as a comparison-methodology false positive; power-cycle rule codified), DEC-0029 (sprite mode 2 attribute masking — all MSX2 sprites were invisible), DEC-0030 (fMSX 6.0 registered as the independent second behavior reference), DEC-0031 (boot logo: #F4 register + line-granular collision + pre-armed COL transfer + a latent OOB crash; border composition), DEC-0032 (V99x8 color-0 transparency; border made opt-in per human preference), DEC-0033 (exact audio pacing: bounded ~40 ms latency, authentic 59.9227 Hz frame rate). Every fix universal, hardware-grounded, QA-passed (two Conditional-Pass-then-fixed among the wider day, all others clean/unconditional), all discovered through the human's own live play — the project's first sustained human-in-the-loop QA phase, and its most productive defect-finding method to date. Standing process changes ratified during the arc: universal-fixes-only; RC-checkpoint-only ZEXALL cadence (with the cpu/core carve-out); the openMSX-vs-fMSX disagreement-arbitration discipline.
- Impacted Milestones: Backlog **C5 → DONE (DEC-0034)** — the last of Section B's C-rows other than C10 (deferred → M31) to close. Remaining open backlog after this arc: C1/D4 (blocked pending an independent source), C10→M31, E1→M30, F1→M32, F2→M33, G1→M29, G2/G3/G4 (indefinite). Next natural milestone: the human's earlier "production-candidate around M30" framing — M29 (SCC) and/or M30 (YM2413 FM synthesis, the biggest audible gap) as the road there, with the RC-checkpoint ZEXALL sweep at that gate.
- Risk Notes: (1) The MSXDOS.SYS-to-`A>` handoff question is the one narrow, named residual from C5's closure — a candidate check for any future disk-fidelity cycle (M31). (2) The M28 C5 system test's name/assertions now document a superseded negative finding under an artificial loop shape — re-baselining or renaming it is a hygiene candidate for the next milestone that touches that area. (3) YS II's two-disk set will eventually exercise live disk SWAPPING, which has no UI/CLI mechanism yet — a genuine future feature need, noted (not scheduled).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-09

- Decision ID: DEC-0035

Once we get this fixed and working then we can go into YM2413 FM Synthesis (which will be then M31) as release-candidate. let's continue running autonomously without stopping for my sign off. no slow sweep test until the M31 qa-sign off finishes" (2026-07-09).

  - **M29 — KonamiSCC mapper + SCC/SCC+ wavetable audio chip (backlog G1)**, per the M28 planner's own precondition: a dedicated `references/fact-sheets/` SCC entry is commissioned FIRST (grounded in the independent, public, community-measurement sources — the same class as the YM2413 sheet's own citations — with openMSX `SCC.cc`/`RomKonamiSCC.cc` as primary behavior reference and fMSX `EMULib/SCC.c` as the independent cross-check). Standard planner→developer→QA cycle; tag v1.0.30 on close.

MANDATED FIRST STEP (the human's own instruction, guarding against their own possibly-wrong mapper hypothesis): try loading the ROM on the CURRENT build with each existing mapper type (M19 loaded this file only as a non-identity-claiming Generic8kB mechanical fixture — its REAL mapper type was never established). If a correct mapper type simply works, the universal/system-wide fix is cartridge-identification (backlog G2 territory — e.g. SHA-based identification against locally-present databases and/or a heuristic, never a game-keyed tweak); if no mapper works, a genuine mapper-behavior defect hunt follows. Universal-fix directive applies in full.

C1/D4, C10→(now M32-era), F1/F2, G3/G4 sequencing unchanged in substance; numeric owners for C10/F1/F2 shift back one (M32/M33/M34) and will be re-recorded at their own kickoffs.

(2) M29's SCC fact-sheet must be genuinely independently grounded — the license-sensitive-scope directive fully applies to both openMSX and fMSX sources. (3) The Aleste-2 first-step probe may trivially resolve M30 into a G2 identification milestone — the planner must scope AFTER the probe result is known, not before.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-09
