- Decision ID: DEC-0036
- Requested By: DEC-0035 autonomous-run authorization (human, 2026-07-09).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), on QA's Conditional Pass (`docs/m29-qa-signoff.md`) resolved via the fix-re-confirm-then-proceed pattern (no human stop, per DEC-0035).
- Decision: CLOSE **M29 (backlog G1 — KonamiSCC mapper + Konami SCC 5-channel wavetable chip)**, tag **v1.0.30**. Deliverables: `references/fact-sheets/Konami SCC.md` (grounded entirely in independent community measurements — De Schrijder 2003, Pazos 2003, NYYRIKKI 2005, enen — with SEVEN openMSX-vs-fMSX disagreements recorded and arbitrated per DEC-0030, each corroborated; coordinator independently re-verified the key citations in both references); `src/devices/audio/scc_wavetable.{h,cpp}` (plain SCC: De Schrijder AmpOut=640+Σ mixing law with truncate-before-sum reproduced as a literal unit oracle; (period+1) dividers with period<9 stop; NYYRIKKI latching/restart; Pazos deformation register incl. read-as-write-0xFF; enen power-on state; Mode::Real-only dispatch, G5-ready); `src/devices/cartridge/cartridge_konami_scc_rom.{h,cpp}` (banks 5000/7000/9000/B000 in 0x800 windows, masked (v&0x3F)==0x3F enable, both-effects 0x9000 write, 9800-9FFF window via addr&0xFF, opposite-of-plain-Konami mirroring — verified line-for-line against RomKonamiSCC.cc by developer AND QA); `CartridgeMapperType::KonamiSCC` + CLI "KonamiSCC"; machine `scc_chip()` accessor; SDL3-independent `src/frontend/machine_audio_mixer.{h,cpp}` with **AudioPacer/PsgAudioPump byte-for-byte untouched** (git-diff-proven) and the zero-SCC BYTE-IDENTITY regression oracle (QA-judged sound: the oracle's reference side is the literal pre-M29 arithmetic against byte-frozen shared components). - Decision ID: DEC-0039
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-09), after first-hand playtest of the v1.0.32 production candidate with Aleste 2 (4 screenshots provided). Explicit selection: "M32: both fixes".
- Approved By: Human (milestone authorization); MSX Master Agent (coordinator) executing.
- Decision: OPEN **M32 — the RC-playtest defect pair**, tag target **v1.0.33**. Playtest triage (coordinator, evidence-grounded): the human CONFIRMED the DEC-0033 sound-delay fix in live play; Aleste 2 intro cutscene, title, weapon-select, and game-over screens all render pixel-perfect; the ONE broken screen is the vertically-scrolling gameplay screen (HUD rows intact, playfield garbage), and FM BGM is inaudible while PSG sound effects are audible. **Defect A (universal, renderer architecture): mid-frame VDP register changes are unrepresentable** — `Hbf1xvMachine::render_frame()` (src/machine/hbf1xv_machine.cpp:617) renders all lines from a single register snapshot; Aleste 2 (like most MSX2/2+ action titles) rewrites R#23 from a line-interrupt handler mid-frame to fix the HUD and scroll the playfield (a screen split). Consequence exactly matches the screenshot: HUD correct, scroll ring-buffer shown un-rotated (garbage) below. R#23 support itself is correct and tested (vdp_frame_renderer.cpp:130). Fix direction: per-line rendering — accumulate the frame scanline-by-scanline as the raster advances, reading LIVE registers at each line (openMSX PixelRenderer model, references/openmsx-21.0/src/video/PixelRenderer.cc; DEC-0031's line-granular collision + VdpRasterClock are existing groundwork). NOT a game patch — benefits every split-screen title. **Defect B (universal, mixing policy): FM ~29 dB under PSG** — the FM chain is fully functional (bios/f1xvmus.rom "APRLOPLL"@0x18 in slot 3-3, game detects and keys the chip — M31 evidence), but kFmAmplitudeScale=5 (machine_audio_mixer.h) yields a measured FM contribution peak of 900 / mean-nonzero 261 on the ±32,767 scale (coordinator-measured from the COMMITTED m31-fm-aleste-fmON/fmOFF.wav pair) vs PSG effects at 24,800. openMSX's Sony_HB-F1XV.xml balances PSG:MSX-MUSIC at volume 21000:9000 (~7 dB). Fix direction: re-derive the FM scale from the reference ratio + an A/B loudness comparison of the same deterministic sequence; a machine-level policy correction applied identically to all software (universal-fixes-only memory honored).
- Impacted Milestones: M32 opened (planner-first cycle; planner → developer → QA → coordinator closure). C10's informal "M32-era" label shifts by one (C10→M33-era, F1→M34-era, F2→M35-era) — recorded here, ledger rows updated at M32 closure. ZEXALL/ZEXDOC: NOT planned for M32 (no src/devices/cpu/ or src/core/ touch anticipated; if the renderer work unexpectedly touches core scheduling, the carve-out triggers one immediate sweep per the standing cadence memory).
- Risk Notes: (1) Defect A is an architecture change to the render path — the planner must define hard regression oracles proving all existing frame evidence (boot logo, Metal Gear, Konami splash, DOS/BASIC screens) stays byte-identical for register-static frames. (2) Defect B's exact constant requires an honest derivation, not a to-taste tweak; the §7 "blend ratio varies by machine" fact-sheet note plus the openMSX volume ratio are the grounding. (3) Sprite engine already consumes R#23 per-line (sprite_engine.cpp:126) — the split must keep sprites and background consistent per line.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-09

- Decision ID: DEC-0043
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-09), two live-playtest reports on v1.0.33/v1.0.34 with the explicit standing directive re-affirmed: "REMEMBER our RULE. we are not just doing in-place patches... understand the systematic issue and address it universally and holistically."
- Approved By: Human (the reports + directive are the charter); MSX Master Agent (coordinator) executing.
- Decision: (1) **R-M32-7 CLOSED — PASS.** The human's verdict on the M32 fixes, verbatim: "absolutely gold! game play perfectly, music and sound effects are all correct!" (Aleste 2: gameplay, FM BGM, and effects all confirmed by ear at k=21; DEC-0040's final acceptance signal delivered). (2) OPEN **M34 — the playtest defect pair** (tag target v1.0.35), both COORDINATOR-TRIAGED to root cause with evidence before this entry: **Defect A (audio, universal): PSG point-sampling aliasing makes real-hardware-inaudible ultrasonic tones LOUDLY audible.** Repro: Aleste 2 title→weapon-select transition, "high pitch beee bbee bip". Coordinator probe evidence (temporary --aleste-beep-probe on the recorded m32 smoke recipe, three identical deterministic runs with per-source muting, REVERTED after capture per the m31/m32 probe precedent): frames 2190-2299 carry a ~20.6 kHz near-Nyquist tone at RMS up to 17,533 (LOUDER than the actual music) that is 100% PSG (FM diff rms=21, SCC diff rms=0); PSG registers in the window: R0/R1=R2/R3=R4/R5=0 (tone period 0 on ALL channels), R7=0xB8 (all three tones ENABLED), R8/R9 volume-modulated 7-15 (the audible "bbee bbee" gating). Tone period 0 on a real YM2149 degenerates to ~112 kHz — inaudible and smoothed to DC by the analog output stage; the game's behavior is CORRECT (a standard silence idiom). Our defect: PsgAudioPump/SccWavetable point-sample the chip level once per 81-cycle window, so >Nyquist content aliases into the audible band. Universal fix direction: band-limited per-sample production — integrate (box-average) the chip output across the 81-cycle sample window, modeling the analog reconstruction (openMSX equivalent: native-rate generation + filtered resampling); applies identically to PSG and SCC by construction; FM already generates at native 49716 Hz. NOTE: this deliberately changes output PCM bytes — every byte-identity audio oracle (M26/M29/M31/M32 lineage) must be re-baselined through planner/QA discipline, never silently. **Defect B (video, universal): the background renderer ignores R#1 bit6 (BL, display-enable).** Repro: Metal Gear room transitions show a line-by-line "slow fill" of half-rewritten VRAM ("negative-color" upper half — color table lagging pattern table). Coordinator evidence: vdp_frame_renderer.cpp contains ZERO reads of control_register(1)/BL — content renders regardless of blanking — while sprite_engine.cpp:90 DOES honor the same bit (an internal asymmetry proving the gap); on real hardware BL=0 shows the backdrop color across the active area (openMSX PixelRenderer displayEnabled semantics). The M32 per-line renderer did not cause this — it exposed a gap present since M20 (snapshot rendering flashed the same in-progress state whole-frame). In-milestone verification required: instrument the recorded Metal Gear recipe for R#1 BL=0 windows around a room transition + openMSX A/B of the same scripted transition (if the A/B shows real hardware ALSO displays the progressive fill in some phase, record the honest disposition and scope the fix to exactly what the reference corroborates).
- Impacted Milestones: M34 opened (planner-first cycle). Both defects touch NO src/devices/cpu/ or src/core/ files — ZEXALL stays withheld per the standing cadence (tripwire stands).
- Risk Notes: (1) The audio-oracle re-baseline is the highest-discipline item — the planner must enumerate every affected byte-oracle test and define the new grounding (a band-limited reference computation, not frozen bytes). (2) Defect B's fix must keep the M32 static-frame byte-identity for BL=1 frames (the blanked-line path is additive). (3) The band-limit must preserve determinism (integer arithmetic; no floats in the sample loop if the existing pipeline is integer).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-09

- Decision ID: DEC-0050
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-10), during M36 SRAM analysis: "you are developing true sony's
  hbf1xv msx2+ which has built in FM. you need to decide, as per system spec officially, you need
  to implement SRAM as peripheral or internal component." Also: "you can create some formatted disk
  to test save feature of the ysII if it can really write to a disk." Chose FM-PAC-peripheral +
  spec-clarification via AskUserQuestion.
- Approved By: Human; MSX Master Agent (coordinator), grounded in the authoritative reference.
- Decision: **ARCHITECTURAL — the HB-F1XV's built-in FM is MSX-MUSIC (OPLL YM2413 + BIOS, NO SRAM),
  NOT a Panasonic FM-PAC.** GROUNDING (authoritative): `references/openmsx-21.0/share/machines/
  Sony_HB-F1XV.xml` declares `<MSX-MUSIC>` (rom + `<ym2413-core>`) with **no** `<sramname>` — while
  every SRAM-bearing device in that same file has an explicit `<sramname>` (S1985, RTC/cmos,
  MSX-JE); the real `f1xvmus.rom` is the "APRLOPLL" MSX-MUSIC BIOS. Consequences: **(1)** "NO S-RAM
  AVAILABLE" is CORRECT hardware behavior on a bare HB-F1XV — the YS II symptom is NOT an internal-
  FM defect. **(2) SRAM = PERIPHERAL**: the 8 KB battery SRAM belongs to the Panasonic FM-PAC
  CARTRIDGE (external, insertable), not the machine. **(3) M36 Bug-A REFRAMED** (supersedes the M36
  planner package's machine-level SRAM framing): implement the FM-PAC as a NEW insertable cartridge
  peripheral — new `CartridgeMapperType::FmPac` (ROM-bank window at 0x4000-0x5FFF + 8 KB battery
  SRAM + 0x5FFE/0x5FFF magic unlock + bank register, per `references/openmsx-21.0/src/sound/
  MSXFmPac.cc`), loadable via `--cart` exactly like plugging an FM-PAC into real hardware; YS II
  S-RAM save then works WHEN the FM-PAC cartridge is inserted. **(4)** The emulator's speculative
  internal 8 KB `sram_` (`hbf1xv_machine.h:176-179`, added on a guessed assumption) is an
  INACCURACY to reconcile — remove from the bare machine / relocate into the FM-PAC peripheral.
  **(5)** CLAUDE.md SOUND spec-table row clarified (built-in = MSX-MUSIC no-SRAM; FM-PAC w/ SRAM =
  optional peripheral). **(6) DISK-SAVE PATH (human-suggested test):** independent of the FM-PAC
  work, verify whether the emulator can actually WRITE to a disk image — create a FORMATTED blank
  720 KB disk and drive YS II's "DISK" save to it, confirming the write persists back to the `.dsk`
  file. FIRST determine (system-wide, per feedback_system_wide_review_first) whether the FDC write
  PATH exists: WD2793 WRITE SECTOR/WRITE TRACK command handling → DRQ → DiskDrive/DiskImage write →
  flush-to-host-file. If any stage is read-only/stubbed, disk save is an IMPLEMENT task, not just a
  verify.
- Impacted Milestones: M36 Phase 2A REFRAMED (FM-PAC peripheral cartridge). NEW M36 work item:
  disk-write capability verify/implement + a formatted-blank-disk test asset/tool. Dependency: an
  FM-PAC BIOS ROM asset (Panasonic SW-M004) is needed for the peripheral's real-software validation
  — human to provide. Applies feedback_system_wide_review_first (peripheral-vs-internal + slot/
  memory decode + the full FDC write pipeline are whole-system decisions).
- Risk Notes: (1) The FM-PAC cartridge's 0x4000-0x5FFF window is shared (ROM banks vs unlock-gated
  SRAM) inside its slot — route reads/writes correctly, coexist with #A8 + the memory-mapper, and
  do NOT regress the built-in MSX-MUSIC (stays SRAM-less) or other cartridges. (2) Disk WRITE may
  be unimplemented in the current FDC/DiskImage layer (to be checked) — if so it's real device work
  (WD2793 write commands + image write-back + host-file flush), NOT a quick fix. (3) FM-PAC BIOS
  ROM asset dependency gates the peripheral's real-software validation.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-10

- Decision ID: DEC-0051
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-10), after YS II did not recognize the blank formatted save disk ("it does not work. ysII does not seem to recognize the save disk"): "let's park this and implement a new feature. with --snapshot option, if i hit F12, it captures exact state of every component into a disk debug/snapshot/ folder." Scope confirmed via AskUserQuestion = CAPTURE-ONLY, comprehensive (NOT a reload/resume save-state this cycle).
- Approved By: Human; MSX Master Agent (coordinator).
- Decision: NEW FEATURE -- a comprehensive, live-triggerable DEBUG SNAPSHOT capability, structured as **M36 Phase 3** (debug snapshot tooling), a sibling of Phase 1 (playtest harness). (1) A host hotkey **F12** in the SDL3 frontend captures the EXACT current state of EVERY machine component to `debug/snapshot/<id>/` (typed dump per component), and a `--snapshot` CLI option enables/points the capture (headless trigger + output-dir control). (2) SCOPE = CAPTURE-ONLY (inspection). NO reload/resume this cycle -- but the serialization must be RESTORE-READY so a future save-state can layer on without a rewrite. (3) COMPREHENSIVE component set (beyond the existing CPU/RAM/VRAM/SRAM state-dump): CPU (all regs incl. shadow/IX/IY/I/R/IFF/IM/PC/SP/WZ/Q), memory-mapper 64KB RAM + segment regs, 128KB VRAM, V9958 register file R#0-46 + status + address latch + palette + command-engine + sprite + raster clock, PSG/YM2149, YM2413 OPLL (+ inserted FM-PAC OPLL), RTC/RP5C01, FDC WD2793 + drive + inserted-disk index, S1985 backup RAM, slot/subslot selection (#A8/#FFFF), cartridge mapper state (banks, FM-PAC SRAM + unlock latch), Halnote/MSX-JE mapper + its SRAM, pause/speed/Ren-Sha, scheduler/clock/cycle counters. (4) EXTENDS the existing `serialize_state_dump()` / `--dump-state` foundation; ADDITIVE + read-only w.r.t. emulation (add const getters where a device's internal state is not yet exposed; NO behavior change, NO cpu/core timing edit -> ZEXALL withheld). (5) DETERMINISTIC: the snapshot CONTENT for an identical run to the same frame/cycle must be byte-identical (auditable); prefer a deterministic snapshot id (frame/cycle or monotonic index) over wall-clock for reproducibility (a wall-clock folder name is acceptable only if content stays reproducible). (6) PRIMARY NEAR-TERM PAYOFF: capture the exact machine state at the YS II building-entry BLACK SCREEN (Bug B, the M36 mandatory item) to root-cause it (VDP blank vs FDC read-fail vs slot/mapper) WITHOUT depending on the game's own save.
- Impacted Milestones: M36 gains Phase 3 (debug snapshot). Bug B repro pivots to snapshot-based root-cause (the save-disk approach is PARKED). R-M35-1 + the 5 completed Phase-2 slices remain uncommitted, carried to M36 closure.
- Note (YS II save disk, PARKED per the human): YS II shows "NO S-RAM AVAILABLE" -> its primary save target is very likely FM-PAC battery SRAM, not an arbitrary data disk; a blank FAT12 disk is not recognized because YS II either saves only to FM-PAC SRAM or expects its own save-disk format. Likely-correct save path = insert the M36 FM-PAC cartridge (`--cart roms/fmpac.rom`); to be confirmed later (it is the M36 "FM-PAC S-RAM saves work" clause). NOT a defect in the M36-S-c disk-write pipeline (that is byte-level test-proven, independent of YS II's own save behavior).
- Risk Notes: (1) "Every component" is broad -- some devices may not expose full state via const getters yet; adding them is additive/read-only but touches each device header (system-wide review first). (2) Determinism: the snapshot writer must not perturb emulation or consume RNG/wall-clock for content. (3) Restore-ready format now, but restore itself is explicitly OUT of scope (deferred) to bound effort. (4) F12 must not collide with an existing SDL3 binding (F11 = disk-swap).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-10

- Decision ID: DEC-0052
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-10), during the M36 Bug B crash diagnosis (the DSKCHG fix did not resolve the freeze; the post-fix snapshot shows a CONTROL-FLOW CRASH -- PC=399B in a zeroed NOP field, SP=0xA56C pointing into loaded data, not a valid stack): "add a feature to stream-capture (full system dump at every tick of the system) by hitting F10 (toggle on and off). i will toggle it on as i enter the building. since the game stops at the point with a black screen, we may have better clue what happens."
- Approved By: Human; MSX Master Agent (coordinator).
- Decision: NEW debug feature -- **live STREAM-CAPTURE**, an extension of the M36 Phase 3 snapshot + M27 CPU-trace tooling, to capture the TEMPORAL evolution into the YS II building-entry crash (a single snapshot shows only the end state). Design (practical realization of "full dump every tick" -- a literal per-CPU-cycle full dump is ~GB/s and would stall the emulator, so "tick" = frame + an instruction-level trace ring): (1) **F10** in the SDL3 frontend TOGGLES stream-capture on/off (host hotkey like F11=swap/F12=snapshot; never routed to the input mapper). (2) While ON: write a FULL snapshot every FRAME (reuse debug_snapshot write_snapshot) into debug/snapshot/stream_<id>/f<frame>_c<cycle>/ -- the frame-by-frame state evolution. (3) ALSO maintain an in-memory per-instruction CPU-trace RING buffer (PC/opcode/regs/SP), hooked at the MACHINE level (step_cpu_instruction), reusing the M27 write_cpu_trace facility -- NOT cpu-core, so ZEXALL stays withheld. (4) AUTO-STOP + finalize (dump the trace ring to debug/traces/ + a final full snapshot) the instant the CPU HALTs (crash), so the user need not time the toggle-off. (5) Additive/default-off (no F10 = byte-for-byte unchanged), deterministic content. PURPOSE: localize the M36 Bug B control-flow crash -- find when the stack is corrupted / PC derails during the interior load.
- Impacted Milestones: M36 Phase 3 gains the stream-capture extension. Bug B diagnosis pivots to stream-capture (the DSKCHG read-and-clear fix stays -- it corrected a genuine latent media-change bug + strengthened R-M35-1 -- but was NOT the freeze cause; the real cause is a control-flow crash still under investigation).
- Risk Notes: (1) Per-frame full snapshots are ~200KB x 60/s -- feasible for a short toggle window; the trace ring is bounded in-memory (dumped on halt). (2) The trace hook must stay at the machine level (no Z80-core edit) to keep ZEXALL withheld. (3) F10 must not collide with an existing SDL3 binding (F11/F12 taken; verify F10 free).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-10

---

- Decision ID: DEC-0053
- Requested By: Coordinator disposition after the M36 Bug B deep-forensics + device-timing A/B audit (2026-07-10), the human having authorized autonomous end-to-end operation and gone away.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator). Human ratification pending on return.
- Decision: **M36 Bug B (YS II building-interior black screen) is ROOT-CAUSED and remains OPEN.** It is a FAITHFUL nested VBLANK-interrupt storm, NOT an emulator defect in the crashing path: the game installs its MINIMAL ISR (0xA5E3), which runs the shared sound routine 0xA352 with the EI at 0xA373 UNPATCHED and reads VDP S#2 (never S#0), so the VBLANK F flag is never acknowledged -> the EI re-fires the interrupt ~440x mid-ISR -> stack overflow -> corrupted return address -> PC executes graphics data as code -> stray 0x76 HALT with IFF1=0 -> permanent freeze. Our V9958 interrupt path was AUDITED and is CORRECT vs openMSX (VBLANK F set only when IE0 enabled; /INT level-held until S#0 read; S#0-read clears F; S#2-read does not) -- a real V9958+Z80 crashes identically in this state. Disk reads are BYTE-PERFECT (12/12 sector CRCs match disk2.dsk). The storm CONDITION is assembled UNCONDITIONALLY by the game's own B282 handler (install minimal ISR at B297; load with IE0 OFF at B2A0; arm the sound path (A5E1)>=0x18 at B2AB; re-enable IE0) -- there is NO device-read-gated branch in the captured window, and the full-ISR restore (0xAAB4 -> writes A5F5 to 0x0039) NEVER executes (0 hits in the 1M-instruction trace). Therefore the TRUE divergence is UPSTREAM of the captured window (before ~frame 2282): on real hardware the game should not be in this scene / processing this RAM-script command (mem[0x1021]=0x02 -> B282) here.
- Device-timing A/B (WD2793 + VDP command-engine vs references/openmsx-21.0): the ONLY concrete accuracy gap found is **WD2793 has NO rotational latency** -- our begin_read_sector uses a fixed ~228-cycle DRQ delay, whereas openMSX schedules the first DRQ at the sector's index-pulse-relative rotational arrival (WD2793.cc type2Loaded:544 / type2Search:557 / startReadSector:624). This is a GENUINE fidelity defect (tracked as a separate accuracy follow-on, NEW backlog item), but the audit assessed it is NOT the Bug B cause (the load self-synchronizes on DRQ polling, ran entirely IE0-OFF, byte-perfect, and the storm is armed unconditionally regardless of load duration). INTRQ/BUSY-on-completion timing and VDP S#2 CE both MATCH openMSX -- no storm-relevant discrepancy.
- DECISION: do NOT land a speculative device fix (respect the audit's confirm-before-fix guidance + the standing no-oracle-weakening / protect-the-FDC-timing-oracles discipline). Bug B closure needs data that REQUIRES the human: (1) an earlier/wider F10 trace starting BEFORE the scene-entry (to capture the upstream deciding branch + writes to 0x0039/(A5E1)/VDP R1 + FDC/VDP I/O), and/or (2) an openMSX A/B of the identical scene (WSL openMSX 19.1 CONFIRMED available) to establish whether real hardware even processes this script command here and, if so, what routes it to the full-ISR restore. BOTH require the human to drive YS II to the building -- it is NOT headlessly reproducible (no crashing input log exists; autonomous navigation stalls at the guarded starting area, the same wall the developer hit).
- Impacted Milestones: M36 -- Phase 2 device features + Phase 3 debug tools DONE, committed as WIP checkpoint af44cb3, QA CONDITIONAL PASS (docs/m36-qa-signoff.md); the mandatory completion item (Bug B) OPEN. M36 NOT tagged (v1.0.37 withheld -- the milestone's own goal is not met). NEW accuracy backlog item: WD2793 read rotational latency.
- Risk Notes: (1) The WD2793 rotational-latency fix, if later pursued, is a delicate high-risk FDC-timing change requiring faithful re-derivation of the M16 timing oracles + an openMSX read-timing A/B -- do NOT weaken oracles to pass. (2) Bug B end-to-end verification requires the human's live YS II re-run to the building (the M35 live-validation precedent).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-10

- Decision ID: DEC-0054
- Requested By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), M36 closure after the repo owner LIVE-validated YS II fully playable (building interiors load + saves persist) on the real SDL3 build.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator release decision), on the QA PASS (docs/m36-qa-signoff-final.md) + live human validation.
- Decision: **M36 CLOSED (tag v1.0.37, 2026-07-10).** The completion criterion is MET: "YS II fully playable like real hardware -- building interiors load, FM-PAC S-RAM saves work (peripheral cart) AND/OR disk saves persist -- verified by msx-playtest" -- LIVE human-validated (the owner entered a building interior which now RENDERS, and confirmed FM-PAC saving works; both save paths persist). Deliverables: Phase 1 (msx-playtest observe-act-replay harness), Phase 2 (DEC-0050 device work: FM-PAC peripheral cartridge, disk-save persistence, speculative sram_ removal, R-M35-1, DSKCHG read-and-clear), Phase 3 (DEC-0051/0052 debug tooling: F12 comprehensive snapshot, F10 live stream-capture + the lightweight watch mode), the **Bug B fix**, and **SDL3 FM-PAC SRAM persistence**.
- **Bug B FIX (the mandatory item) -- SUPERSEDES DEC-0053's "V9958 interrupt path is correct" conclusion.** Bug B was a FAITHFUL-looking nested VBLANK-interrupt storm, but the actual cause is a real V9958 interrupt-accuracy bug: `V9958Vdp::change_register` (R#0/R#1) did NOT re-evaluate /INT on an IE1/IE0 write, so when YS II's building-load ISR cleared IE0 (writing R#1=0x40), our /INT stayed asserted (the VBlank F flag was still latched) and the ISR's trailing EI re-fired the interrupt ~440x -> stack overflow -> crash. FIXED per references/openmsx-21.0/src/video/VDP.cc:1177-1198 (IE0 clear -> irq_vertical_ reset; IE0 set -> set iff F pending; IE1 clear -> irq_horizontal_ reset; then update_irq()). The DEC-0053 audit checked the S#0-read /INT path but MISSED this register-write path. The bug was pinned by the human's F10 lightweight-watch-mode capture (the watchlog showed the ISR's repeated R#1=0x40 writes). Evidence: non-vacuous unit test (video_v9958_ie0_register_write_irq), interrupt-seam regressions clean (interrupt_ack, v9958_status_irq, m26_vsync, m32_line_interrupt, m34_bl_latch), openMSX VDP-IRQ runtime A/B on the genuine Sony_HB-F1XV (0->1->0->1 IRQvertical pattern, independently re-run by QA), register/VRAM parity empty-diff, and LIVE human validation.
- **FM-PAC SRAM persistence** completed for the SDL3 build (was headless-only): auto-save to <cart-ROM>.sram (load-on-insert + flush-on-exit), --fmpac-sram override, --no-fmpac-sram opt-out; round-trip integration-tested (frontend_sdl3_app_fmpac_sram_integration_test).
- **QA: PASS** (docs/m36-qa-signoff-final.md) -- clean-rebuild 207/207 (Bug B) then 208/208 (with FM-PAC persistence); zero src/devices/cpu + src/core edits (ZEXALL correctly withheld); source parity vs VDP.cc:1177-1198 line-for-line; non-vacuous adversarial mutation restored byte-identical; independent openMSX VDP-IRQ runtime A/B.
- **R3 A/B WAIVER** (per the final QA recommendation): the behavior-critical VDP change carries a first-hand openMSX runtime A/B + empty-diff register/VRAM parity -- its A/B requirement is satisfied by evidence, not waived. FM-PAC + DSKCHG rest on source parity (vs MSXFmPac.cc / DiskChanger.cc:95-100 / PhilipsFDC.cc:37,90) + unit/integration tests + the live human save-persist run; the dedicated FM-PAC (AC-d8) / DSKCHG (AC-b6) runtime smokes are DEFERRED as post-tag release-candidate hardening.
- Residual (non-blocking, carried forward): R-A WD2793 read rotational latency (NEW accuracy backlog, DEC-0053; audit-assessed NOT the Bug B cause -- a delicate FDC-timing follow-on); R-B commit a tools/ VDP-IRQ probe harness for reproducibility; R-C FM-PAC .sram on-disk format differs from openMSX (interchange-only); R-D FM-PAC OPLL audio not yet mixed into the machine output (opll() seam present); R-E roms/fmpac.rom is a signature-valid non-canonical FM-PAC BIOS variant (validated functionally, not by hash).
- Impacted Milestones: M36 DONE, tag v1.0.37. The DEC-0035..0054 autonomous arc (M29 v1.0.30 ... M35 v1.0.36 ... M36 v1.0.37) reaches the human's end goal: YS II fully playable like real hardware.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-10

- Decision ID: DEC-0056
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-10), post-v1.0.37, two live-play feature requests: (1) "i want to have cli option --speed that ranges from any range the hardware specifies to the emulator" (the Sony hardware Speed Controller); (2) "is this possible to scale current SDL3 window to bigger size ... proper scaling, so that i can play the game in bigger window (even full screen) ... with smooth aliasing or something".
- Approved By: Human (requested); MSX Master Agent (coordinator) -- folded into the open M37 hardening cycle as two additional frontend slices D + E.
- Decision: **Add M37 Slice D (--speed CLI) and Slice E (SDL3 window scaling/fullscreen); tag target v1.0.38 now covers all five slices A-E.** Both are frontend-only (expect ZERO src/devices/cpu / src/core edits -> ZEXALL withheld).
  **(D) `--speed <0..7>` CLI (headless + SDL3):** wire the EXISTING M25 `devices::chipset::Mb670836PauseController` (src/devices/chipset/mb670836_pause.h) to a launch-time initial speed level via `machine.pause_controller().set_speed_level(N)`. CLARIFICATION for the human: the Sony HB-F1XV "Speed Controller" is a CPU SLOW-DOWN duty cycle (a difficulty aid), NOT a clock/turbo speed-up -- level 0 = full speed (default, byte-identical to today), kMaxSpeedLevel=7 = maximum slow-motion (CPU paused 7 of every 8 VBlanks). Range 0..7 is the M25 design-default duty-cycle range (A-M25-3), not a precisely-measured analog-slider fact. The existing SDL3 F6/F7 runtime stepping (sdl3_input_mapper.cpp) is UNCHANGED; --speed only sets the initial value. Parse-error on out-of-range/non-numeric (mirrors --max-frames policy). If the human later wants a genuine host fast-forward/turbo (a non-hardware convenience), that is a SEPARATE future feature, not this slice.
  **(E) SDL3 window scaling + fullscreen (SDL3 only; headless has no window):** (1) make the window RESIZABLE (add SDL_WINDOW_RESIZABLE) so drag-resize scales live; (2) aspect-correct, never-distorted scaling via SDL_SetRenderLogicalPresentation(renderer, 320, 240, SDL_LOGICAL_PRESENTATION_LETTERBOX) -- 320x240 = the MSX 4:3 framing, so the picture is the SAME as today, just bigger/undistorted at any window or fullscreen size; (3) configurable texture filter via SDL_SetTextureScaleMode -- `--filter <nearest|linear>`, DEFAULT linear (the "smooth aliasing" the human asked for; nearest = crisp pixels for purists); (4) `--scale <N>` initial window size = 320N x 240N, DEFAULT 2 (= today's 640x480, non-regressive), sane range clamp (e.g. 1..8); (5) `--fullscreen` starts fullscreen and Alt+Enter toggles fullscreen at runtime (SDL_SetWindowFullscreen), intercepted in Sdl3App's event loop BEFORE input_mapper dispatch (same guard pattern as F10/F11/F12, sdl3_app.cpp:295-313), so it never leaks into the emulated MSX keyboard (RETURN is a matrix key). Grounding: references/sdl3 (SDL_SetRenderLogicalPresentation / SDL_SetTextureScaleMode / SDL_SetWindowFullscreen). Border mode (--border) composition is unchanged and composes with the new logical presentation.
- Impacted Milestones: M37 (was A/B/C per DEC-0055; now A/B/C/D/E). v1.0.38 tag deferred until D+E land and the single end-of-cycle QA sign-off covers all five slices. Sequencing: D+E (frontend, user-facing, independent of FDC) land BEFORE Slice C (WD2793 read rotational latency, highest regression risk, quarantined last with a human YS II re-verify after).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-10

- Decision: **Backfill the agent-protocol ledger for the v1.0.39 release cycle (the M37→M41 gap).** Reconstructed strictly from git history (`v1.0.38 2e464b7 .. v1.0.39 53e4eaf`), `docs/m39-qa-signoff.md`, `docs/m39-fix-plans.md`, the M38 A/B tooling (`tools/gen-m38-vdp-scroll-cart.py` / `m38-run.ps1` / `m38-ab-diff.py`), and the human's real prior-session requests. Findings (evidence-grounded, NOT invented):
  **There was NO M40** — grep-confirmed zero references anywhere in tests/tools/docs/debug/agent-protocol. The human's "M38-40" was approximate. The cycle = **M38 (horizontal scroll) + M39 (voice + HUD + border), released as v1.0.39**, preceded by a same-day **repo-maintenance sub-phase** (unnumbered).
  **Repo-maintenance sub-phase (2026-07-10, 4 commits, unnumbered):** `ed419cd` docs sync to v1.0.38; `e825b9c` tree-wide source comment tidy (ZERO logic — the SOLE cpu/core touch in the whole cycle, provably comment-only per the M39 QA §2.1); `71b71e1` untrack local-only dev folders from the remote (.claude/agent-protocol/debug/docs/references/tests/tools now local-only, DEC-0044-class); `09d12b5` README rewrite as a focused, de-AI project overview. This discharged the human's "make READMEs consistent + comments concise + folders invisible at remote + hide AI involvement" requests.
  **M38 (`b0db02b`, 2026-07-11) — V9958 bitmap horizontal scroll fix.** MSX2+ scrolling bitmap games (F1 per-scanline road, Laydock 2 split screen) rendered scrambled. Two universal register-level root causes, re-derived from openMSX (understanding only, no code copied): (1) R#27 FINE scroll was wrong-signed + circular-wrapped — correct behaviour is R#26 rotates display LEFT 8px-steps (already right) while R#27 shifts RIGHT 0..7 dots + exposes a left border strip (separate mechanism/sign, VDP.hh:340-342/629-631, SDLRasterizer.cc:464-465, PixelRenderer.cc:586-604); (2) multi-page split-page windowing missing — the coarse-wrap tail must read the ADJACENT even/odd page (p2=p1^1) when isMultiPageScrolling (R#25 bit0 && R#2 bit5), not self-wrap (SDLRasterizer.cc:479-538). Fixed in `vdp_frame_renderer` (split coarse-left / fine-right+border; two-page compose only when multi-page active; single-page byte-identical), applied uniformly G4/G5/G6/G7/YJK/YAE — not game-specific. Verified by a game-free cartridge-ROM video-test harness with per-scenario openMSX A/B (baseline 0.00%): s03/s04/s06 MISMATCH→MATCH, s01-s08/s10/s11 MATCH; s09_yjk carried a 6.25% YJK residual (later root-caused + fixed in M41 as DEF-M41-YJKOFFSET). Human-validated live (Laydock + F1 .omr replay: "the scroll is working!!").
  **M39 (`2405a35`/`7fac03d`/`73968d7`/`53e4eaf`, 2026-07-11) — digitized voice + vertical/HUD framing + border default; TAGGED v1.0.39 at `53e4eaf`.** (1) `2405a35` digitized voice/speech silent (Aleste 2 / Laydock): root cause = audio produced once-per-frame in a batch collapsing sub-frame writes; fixed via **PSG `sync_to_cycle()` sync-before-change** (advance the M34 box-average integral to each write cycle BEFORE mutation) + routed the previously-unmixed 1-bit DAC (PPI port-C bit7 keyclick, additive `ClickDac`); both idle-byte-identical; human-confirmed ("sound works!!!"). (2) `7fac03d` then `73968d7`: border framing — briefly defaulted to the openMSX-matching framed canvas, then REVERTED to bare edge-to-edge (Sony original) per the human's explicit preference ("i prefer non-border like Sony's original"); `--border` now opts IN. (3) `53e4eaf` HUD raster split-boundary: fixed-top-HUD games (Aleste 2 "SC/AREA/ARMO/LEV") had the HUD's bottom ~1px row clipped; the M32 render-sync seam committed mid-frame writes at `sync_to_line(line+1)`, one line early — openMSX rounds with the active-display left margin (PixelRenderer.cc:566-567) → **`line+2`**; a universal raster constant (R#23 splits, R#1 BL bands, palette bars). openMSX 19.1 A/B on the genuine Sony_HB-F1XV (Aleste-2 raw frame 2610) confirms the clipped-row delta → 0. - Decision ID: DEC-0061
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-11, post-v1.0.40): "add option --ram 128, 256, 512" (opt-in extra main RAM to load big games); asked "how far does it go? up to 4M?" — coordinator clarified the internal S1985 mapper caps at 512 KB (5-bit read-back); 1-4 MB is external-RAMPAC-cartridge territory.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), under the human's explicit request. SCOPE CHANGE authorized: adds a NON-STOCK opt-in RAM size while preserving the strict 64 KB spec default.
- Decision: **M42 OPENED — add opt-in `--ram <64|128|256|512>` CLI (headless + SDL3), default 64. Tag target v1.0.41.** The strict target-spec 64 KB main RAM stays the DEFAULT and the only stock configuration; 128/256/512 are explicit opt-in "fully-populated S1985" mods (documented non-stock). Rationale for the 512 KB ceiling: the HB-F1XV S1985 provides 5-bit mapper read-back (`0x80 | seg & 0x1F` == 32 segments × 16 KB = 512 KB), already modeled (s1985_engine.cpp set_readback, mask 0x1F). All four offered sizes (4/8/16/32 segments) are natively probeable within that 5-bit read-back; >512 KB is NOT offered internally (software can't size past 5 bits → would need a wider mapper = an external RAM-expansion cartridge, a separate future milestone). Implementation shape (frontend/machine/devices-memory only — ZERO src/core & src/devices/cpu → ZEXALL withheld per slow-test-cadence):
  1. Parameterize the DRAM region size: `Hbf1xvMachine` kDramBytes (h:187, currently `64*1024`) becomes config-driven from the new CLI value; `dram_` allocated at the configured size (default 64 KB → byte-identical to today).
  2. Parameterize `MemoryMapperRam`: replace the compile-time `kSegments = 4` (memory_mapper_ram.h:63) with a runtime segment count DERIVED from `ram_.size() / kSegmentBytes` (16 KB); `physical_address` folds `segment & (num_segments - 1)` (num_segments is a power of two for all four sizes). No static-method assumption of 4.
  3. **Read-back mask UNCHANGED** — stays the authentic S1985 5-bit 0x1F for ALL sizes (the chip's read-back width does not depend on fitted RAM). RAM detection works via the fold-based segment mirroring (fitted < 32 segments → high segments mirror low, exactly as real hardware), so a stock 64 KB still self-detects as 64 KB and a 512 KB fills all 32 segments distinctly.
  4. CLI parse (both executables): `--ram <64|128|256|512>`, validate the enum (reject other values with a parse error mirroring --max-frames/--speed policy), default 64. Additive ParsedSdl3Cli/Sdl3AppConfig + the headless mode's parser.
- Impacted Milestones: **M42 (new).** Acceptance: default 64 KB path byte-identical (all existing memory/mapper/machine oracles green unchanged); a new mapper-fold test for 128/256/512 (correct segment mirroring + no-mirror at the fitted ceiling); CLI parse tests for the enum + rejection; a smoke boot at --ram 512 (BIOS sizes RAM to 512 KB); clean rebuild + fast ctest; no cpu/core touch (ZEXALL withheld). Owner-run tag+push per DEC-0047. Non-stock sizes clearly labeled in --help + README.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-11

- Decision ID: DEC-0062
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-12): after the FM-PAC `CALL FMPAC` A/B investigation, "yes [fix it]. make sure that persistent SRAM implementation must work. I want to have hardware correct (almost bit by bit parity matching with real parts)." Reaffirmed it is worth doing (a legitimate, well-characterized, high-value accuracy gap = the entire BASIC CALL interface).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), under the human's explicit request. SCOPE: opens a core-touching accuracy milestone; planner-first + system-wide review (memory/slot addressing) per [[feedback_system_wide_review_first]]; universal fix only per [[feedback_universal_fixes_only]].
- Decision: **M43 OPENED — fix the MSX extended-statement (`CALL`) dispatch to expansion ROMs + guarantee FM-PAC persistent SRAM is hardware-bit-exact. Tag target v1.1.0 (minor bump: restores a whole BASIC subsystem).** Root finding (msx-playtest A/B, 2026-07-12, `debug/fmpac-call-ab/`): our engine returns "Syntax error" for EVERY BASIC `CALL` expansion (`CALL MUSIC`, `CALL FMPAC`, ...) on the bare machine AND with the FM-PAC, while openMSX (byte-identical ROMs, identical slot layout) accepts `CALL MUSIC` = `Ok`. **DEF-M43-CALLDISPATCH.** Not user-error and not FM-PAC-specific: `CALL FMPAC` is a genuine statement the FM-PAC firmware defines (STATEMENT handler at ROM 0x4082 string-compares "FMPAC" @0xB3 and launches the "PAC2 BACKUP DATA" manager); `bios/f1xvmus.rom` (built-in MSX-MUSIC, sha1 aad42ba4) shares the MSX-MUSIC CALL table (MUSIC/VOICE/TEMPO/TRANSPOSE/PITCH) with INIT=0. Both rely on the BIOS's PASSIVE slot-scan of `AB` headers + inter-slot dispatch of the STATEMENT handler (RDSLT/CALSLT/ENASLT + the `#FFFF` expanded-subslot readback). That slot-bus inter-slot path is the gap. Our machine DOES map the built-in MSX-MUSIC at slot 3-3 page 1 (hbf1xv_machine.cpp:153, matching Sony_HB-F1XV.xml) and DOES boot Disk-BASIC (slot 3-2, proving SOME expanded-subslot scan works) -- so the exact diverging primitive is NOT yet isolated.
  **Asset note:** the human replaced `roms/fmpac.rom` with the CANONICAL 64 KB Panasonic FM-PAC (sha1 **9d789166**, == openMSX's canonical FM-PAC ROM), superseding the prior non-canonical 16 KB variant (2dc4517e). Our `CartridgeFmPacRom` accepts 1..4 banks (16/32/48/64 KB) and bank-folds `bank_ % num_banks_` (0x7FF7), so it maps all 4 banks. roms/ is gitignored (local asset; no provenance claim).
  **Scope (two hard deliverables):**
  1. **DEF-M43-CALLDISPATCH fix -- UNIVERSAL slot-bus inter-slot correctness.** Diagnostic-FIRST: pinpoint the diverging primitive via a `--trace-cpu` A/B of the identical `CALL MUSIC` keystrokes vs an openMSX CPU trace (RDSLT read-through vs CALSLT execute-through vs the `#FFFF` secondary-slot enumeration). Then fix the SlotBus inter-slot access (RDSLT/WRSLT/CALSLT/ENASLT + `#FFFF` subslot readback) so the real BIOS's passive `CALL`-extension scan enumerates + inter-slot-calls the STATEMENT handler of ANY `AB`-header ROM in every slot/subslot -- built-in MSX-MUSIC (expanded 3-3) AND external cartridge slots (FM-PAC). Generic memory/slot-addressing fix, NOT per-command/per-game. Restores `CALL MUSIC`, `CALL FMPAC`, and the whole FM-BASIC set at once.
  2. **FM-PAC persistent SRAM hardware-bit-exact.** Verify/harden the 8 KB battery SRAM to near-bit-exact real-part parity: the magic unlock (0x5FFE=0x4D 'M' / 0x5FFF=0x69 'i' readback while unlocked), the enable register (0x7FF6, incl. the bit4 force-reset gate), bank (0x7FF7), the SRAM window at 0x4000-0x5FFD, and the host-file persistence (`<cart>.rom.sram`, raw 8 KB, byte-format matching openMSX). MUST work through BOTH the game register-path (already working per the human) AND the newly-enabled `CALL FMPAC` "PAC2 BACKUP DATA" manager path (write via the manager -> persist -> reload -> read back identical). Grounded in openMSX MSXFmPac.cc + an SRAM read/write/persist A/B.
- Impacted Milestones: **M43 (new).** Acceptance: `CALL MUSIC` + `CALL FMPAC` behave as openMSX (Ok / launch the manager), verified by a typed-BASIC A/B; the whole MSX-MUSIC CALL table works; FM-PAC SRAM read/write/persist round-trip bit-identical vs openMSX incl. via CALL FMPAC; NO regression (this touches core slot-addressing -> the FULL ZEXALL/ZEXDOC sweep runs at QA + all memory/slot/boot/disk oracles stay green; system-wide review before code; no oracle weakened). Owner-run tag+push per DEC-0047.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-12

- Decision ID: DEC-0063
- Requested By: Flows from DEC-0062 + the M43 Slice-1 diagnostic + the human's LIVE verification.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator).
- Decision: **M43 RE-SCOPED. (a) DEF-M43-CALLDISPATCH = VOID (no bug).** The Slice-1 diagnostic (`debug/m43-slice1/`) proved the MSX extended-statement (`CALL`) dispatch WORKS at full openMSX parity (VRAM ground-truth: `CALL MUSIC`=Ok, `CALL FMPAC`+cart launches the manager, `CALL SYSTEM`/`CALL FORMAT` reach their handlers); the prior "Syntax error" evidence was a headless frame-capture STALENESS artifact (sealed beam-rastered frame lagging coherent VRAM during rapid type-ahead), NOT a defect. **LIVE HUMAN-CONFIRMED** ("it works like a charm!! music plays"). The slot fabric (`src/devices/chipset/slot_bus.*`) was VERIFIED CORRECT vs openMSX MSXCPUInterface.cc and NOT modified -- the diagnostic-first gate prevented an unnecessary edit to the highest-risk subsystem. Root of the false report: the human's original `CALL FMPAC` failure used the prior NON-CANONICAL 16 KB fmpac.rom variant; swapping to the canonical 64 KB (sha1 9d789166) was the real unlock.
  **(b) NEW DEF-M43-FMPAC-SCREEN (real, root-caused, escalated to the fix slice).** When `CALL FMPAC` launches the FM-PAC's built-in "PAC2 BACKUP DATA / COPR.1988 MATSUSHITA" manager (GRAPHIC2), our engine renders a BLANK backdrop-only screen while openMSX renders the full UI. Pixel-rigorous A/B (`debug/m43-slice2/`): the manager's VDP registers (R#0=02 R#1=60 R#2=06 R#3=FF R#4=03 R#7=05 R#10=00) AND all three VRAM tables (name 0x1800, pattern 0x0000, color 0x2000) are BYTE-FOR-BYTE identical to openMSX; feeding the IDENTICAL VRAM through our decoder = blank, through the openMSX decoder = UI. **Root cause: `src/devices/video/vdp_frame_renderer.cpp` uses an ADDITIVE `base+offset` table-address model where the V9958 uses a TMS9918-legacy AND-MASK model.** `pattern_table_base()` (132-134) returns `R#4<<11` (=0x1800 for R#4=0x03; lands on the name table; correct=0x0000); `color_table_base()` (136-140) returns `(R#10<<14)|(R#3<<6)` (=0x3FC0 for R#3=0xFF; past the color table -> reads backdrop=blank; correct=0x2000). The low bits of R#3/R#4 are legacy mask/mirroring bits, not additive address bits. Grounding: openMSX VDP.cc:1299-1355 (`updateColorBase`/`updatePatternBase` `setMask(base, ~0u<<13)`), VDPVRAM.hh:266-269/153-180 (`readNP` = `data[effectiveBaseMask & index]`), CharacterConverter.cc:275-316 (renderGraphic2). **M41's m2_g2 GRAPHIC2 A/B had a BLIND SPOT** (register values where additive == AND-mask), so it MATCHED while missing this; the fix must re-derive that test to canonical registers (R#4=0x03/R#3=0xFF). This is a UNIVERSAL memory-addressing correction (affects all SCREEN 2/4 content drawn with canonical registers), NOT an FM-PAC patch. NO overlap with the Slice-1 staleness (that is a separate TEXT/G1 frame-timing artifact). `src/devices/video` (NOT cpu/core -> mechanical ZEXALL per-edit trigger does NOT fire; but a full A/B of ALL screen modes is required since the fix touches the shared table-base helpers used by G1/G2/G3/Text2).
  **(c) FM-PAC persistent SRAM bit-exact (DEC-0062 deliverable) STANDS** -- unchanged: openMSX `.sram` format (16-byte "PAC2 BACKUP DATA" header + 8190 bytes, MSXFmPac.cc/SRAM.cc) + LOSSLESS migration of existing raw-8192 saves, verified through the (now-visible) CALL FMPAC manager write->persist->reload round-trip.
- Impacted Milestones: **M43 (re-scoped).** Slice 2 becomes the GRAPHIC2/3 AND-mask addressing fix (mode-aware table masks matching openMSX updateNameBase/updateColorBase/updatePatternBase: G1 color ~0u<<6 / name ~0u<<10; G2/G3 pattern/color ~0u<<13; Text2 color ~0u<<9) -- NOT a G2-only special case; strict superset (every currently-correct mode stays bit-exact); the FM-PAC manager UI renders matching openMSX. Slice 3 = SRAM bit-exact. Acceptance: all screen-mode A/B still MATCH openMSX + the FM-PAC manager renders + SRAM round-trip bit-identical; NO oracle weakened; the m2_g2 test re-derived to canonical registers with proven non-tautology. Tag target v1.1.0. Owner-run tag+push per DEC-0047. Also-noted latent (out of scope, Assumption+verify): `v9958_vdp.cpp change_register()` stores raw register bytes with no per-register write-mask vs openMSX VALUE_MASKS_MSX2 (harmless here: R#10=0).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-12

- Decision ID: DEC-0065
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-12): reported a fast-flickering scrambled band in Laydock 2's top status-HUD (around SCORE) present on our engine but not openMSX; asked for a system-wide review + bit-parity. Chose the **PHASED** fix.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator), under the human's request. SCOPE: opens a VDP render-timing accuracy milestone; planner-first + system-wide review per [[feedback_system_wide_review_first]]; universal fix per [[feedback_universal_fixes_only]].
- Decision: **M44 OPENED — DEF-M44-CMDSYNC: the V9958 command engine writes raster-visible VRAM outside the M32 render-sync seam. PHASED.** Root cause CONFIRMED by the Laydock 2 `.omr` A/B vs openMSX (`debug/laydock2-flicker/`): our engine tears the HUD frame-to-frame while openMSX renders it crisp from the BYTE-IDENTICAL final VRAM — a pure render-OBSERVATION-timing defect (the command engine computes correct final VRAM). Precise mechanism: our 10 VDP commands (HMMV/HMMM/LMMV/LMMM/YMMM/LINE/PSET/POINT/SRCH/ABRT) execute as a single ZERO-CYCLE BURST (`vdp_command_engine.h:35-38`; the `for(;;)` loops in `vdp_command_engine.cpp:362/391/425/519/548...` call `vram_.write()` DIRECTLY), and `VdpVram::write()` (`vdp_vram.h:59`) is a plain store with no timestamp/notify — the command engine holds only a `VdpVram&`, never wired into the M32 render-sync. Laydock 2 draws its page-3 HUD via MANY per-frame blits + displays it through a mid-frame split (R#23=0xA4, R#25=0x03 multi-page); our per-line accumulator commits the HUD scanlines at a patchwork of intermediate blit states → tear whose boundary jitters with beam phase → flicker. openMSX runs the command engine INCREMENTALLY over emulated time: every write via `vram.cmdWrite(addr,val,time)` → `writeCommon` NOTIFIES `bitmapVisibleWindow`/`spriteAttribTable`/`spritePatternTable` BEFORE committing the byte ("draw backlog using old state") — `references/openmsx-21.0/src/video/VDPVRAM.hh:318-322,428,575-593`, `VDPCmdEngine.cc:985-1090`. Systematic sync-gap audit (per the human's "system-wide" ask): CPU-driven paths (VRAM #98, registers #99/#9B/palette #9A, mid-frame R#23/R#18/R#19/R#26/R#27, mode/blink) are ALL correctly synced via the io_write seam (v9958_vdp.cpp:125) — the only gaps are the command engine's own writes (PRIMARY: bitmap-visible VRAM = the Laydock2 cause; SECONDARY latent: sprite attr/pattern tables) and its zero-cycle duration (COUPLED: `CE`/S#2 bit0 clears instantly → busy-wait games issue later register writes at the wrong beam line).
  **PHASE 1 (this milestone, M44, target v1.1.1): the contained flicker fix.** Give the command engine's VRAM writes correct render-OBSERVATION timing so each display row is committed against the correct partial-command state (distribute a command's writes in raster order + route them through the render-sync seam per committed row, mirroring openMSX's cmdWrite→notify) — WITHOUT the full per-mode access-slot cycle model. Removes the visible tear/flicker universally (every command-engine-drawn screen), strict superset (CPU-driven rendering + all currently-correct screen modes stay bit-exact). Wire the render-sync listener (or a VdpVram notify callback) into the command engine. Fix the SECONDARY sprite-table gap in the same seam if cheap.
  **PHASE 2 (tracked follow-on, separate milestone): full command-engine cycle-timing** — incremental `execute*(EmuTime limit)` + access-slot calculator + the `CE`/S#2 duration so busy-wait-on-CE timing is bit-exact (the COUPLED gap). Deferred by the human's phased choice.
- Impacted Milestones: **M44 (new, Phase 1).** `src/devices/video` (command engine + VDP + accumulator wiring) — NOT cpu/core (mechanical ZEXALL per-edit trigger does not fire; but a FULL screen-mode + command-engine A/B is required — high blast radius). Acceptance: Laydock 2 HUD renders crisp/stable matching openMSX (the `.omr` A/B); all M41 screen-mode A/Bs still 0.000%; the M22 sprite-cmd-parity + command-engine oracles stay green or are re-derived (no weakening); non-tautology proven. Owner-run tag+push per DEC-0047.

- Decision ID: DEC-0066

  **Phase 1 (`a27a1c4`, src/devices/video + src/machine only, zero cpu/core):** the command-engine per-row render-sync FOUNDATION (mechanism A: `notify_dest_row` → `on_commit_up_to(L)`, `L=((dy&0xFF)-R#23)&0xFF`; four gates keep it a strict superset). - Decision ID: DEC-0067
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-12): critical report — YS II in-game save to disk2 (with --fast-disk, they believed) produced a corrupt disk that crashes on room entry (SP-underflow), reproduced IDENTICALLY on openMSX (so the corruption is persisted in the .dsk). Demanded a holistic system-architect fix: the WD2793 FDC write must be bit-to-bit accurate to spec, with AND without --fast-disk. Pristine YS2 disks provided at disks/games/ys2-pristine/.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator). CRITICAL data-integrity bug. System-wide review first + universal fix.
- Decision: **M45 OPENED — DEF-M45-WRITEDRQ: the WD2793 accurate-mode write path corrupts normally-timed disk writes.** Root cause CONFIRMED (`debug/fdc-write-investigation/`, real-object harness linking wd2793/disk_drive/disk_image .obj): `Wd2793::write_data` models DRQ as a **free-running absolute-cycle level deadline** (`wd2793.cpp:274-281`, gated `!fast_disk_`); when a CPU data-register write arrives >1 byte-period (114 cyc) past that rigid deadline it substitutes `0x00`+sets LOST_DATA, AND the injected zeros consume `data_available_` so the sector `finish_write_sector`es EARLY → the real tail bytes are silently DROPPED. Signature = dense zeros + shifted survivors + truncated tail — EXACTLY the disk2 corruption (LBA 9/10/11/16 save area, 98-110 injected zeros/sector, LOST_DATA). **This REVERSES the --fast-disk suspicion:** the zero-sub branch is code-gated `!fast_disk_` → IMPOSSIBLE in fast mode; the fast path is byte-perfect under every realistic cadence. The corrupting save therefore ran in ACCURATE (default) timing (--fast-disk defaults OFF + toggles live via Alt+D). A well-behaved BIOS write (DSKIO, interrupts off, tight DRQ poll) is clean in BOTH modes; the accurate zero-sub only fires when the CPU cannot hold the rigid 114-cyc pace — a game write loop with interrupts enabled + a mid-transfer ISR stall (YS II). openMSX's PhilipsFDC models no FDC `/WAIT` (accepts CPU access immediately) yet does NOT corrupt: its WD2793 uses a proper DRQ EDGE-handshake and substitutes 0x00+LOST_DATA only on a genuinely-missed SCHEDULED FSM tick, never on an absolute cumulative deadline, never mode-gated. Ranked divergences vs `references/openmsx-21.0/src/fdc/WD2793.cc`: (1)[ROOT] rigid deadline + inline zero-sub, fast-gated; (2) no edge DRQ↔dataReg handshake / one-byte pipeline (openMSX `setDataReg` :235-247 deasserts DRQ on the CPU write + latches; ours writes straight to buffer on a DRQ LEVEL → timing-drift-sensitive); (3) no first-byte CHECK_WRITE gate (openMSX `checkStartWrite` :674-701 aborts + LOST_DATA writing NOTHING; ours pre-fills 512 zeros + waits → an aborted/late-first-byte write leaves an ALL-ZERO sector). **Fix (universal, spec-accurate, correct WITH and WITHOUT --fast-disk):** re-model the accurate write path to the real-WD2793 / openMSX DRQ edge-handshake + one-byte pipeline + the first-byte CHECK_WRITE gate; substitute 0x00+LOST_DATA ONLY on a genuinely-missed scheduled tick; REMOVE the `!fast_disk_` Lost-Data gate (fast becomes a pure timing-scale of the same correct FSM, NOT a bug-suppressing branch). Resolve the FDC-`/WAIT` question (openMSX doesn't model it; if HB-F1XV doesn't wire it, the handshake fix is sufficient).
  **Forensics:** disk1 == pristine (NOT corrupted → NO mis-addressing/CHS/drive-select/cross-disk bug; `chs_to_lba` correct); disk2 differs in EXACTLY 4 sectors (LBA 9/10/11/16); host-file flush faithful (bytes were already corrupt in memory from the write). **Repair: the human's save is NOT deterministically recoverable** (zero-sub destroyed real bytes + truncated the tail; indistinguishable from genuine zeros). Options: (1) restore pristine `ys2-d2.dsk` over `disk2.dsk` → playable disk, save reverts to initial; (2) human re-saves after the fix (or with --fast-disk, currently immune). No pristine copy of the intended save exists.
- Impacted Milestones: **M45 (new).** `src/devices/fdc/wd2793.*` (± disk_drive) — NOT cpu/core → ZEXALL withheld-substituted; HIGH blast radius (all disk writes) → thorough FDC/disk-save/multi-disk A/B + a NEW drifting/stalling-cadence write test (the existing wd2793_type2/fastdisk tests only use an ideal 1-cyc poll, which is why this was never caught). Acceptance: the stall/drift test reproduces the corruption on the pre-fix code + byte-perfect post-fix in BOTH modes (non-tautology); openMSX write A/B byte-identical; BIOS BSAVE stays byte-perfect (strict superset for the working case); every FDC/disk oracle green. Tag target v1.1.1 (critical data-integrity fix). Owner-run tag+push per DEC-0047.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-12

---

- Decision ID: DEC-0068
- Requested By: Flows from DEC-0067 + the msx-qa M45 sign-off.
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator release decision).
- Decision: **M45 CLOSED — QA CONDITIONAL PASS (`docs/m45-qa-signoff.md`); coordinator release decision: tag v1.1.1 @ `4a8f8e0` GATED on the owner's live YS II re-save-and-load test.** The DEF-M45-WRITEDRQ fix (`4a8f8e0`, `src/devices/fdc/wd2793.{cpp,h}` only, zero cpu/core) is verified: clean from-scratch rebuild; **206/206 headless** (the 14-test delta = SDL3-gated frontend tests, none FDC-related; QA's from-scratch build ran headless because it wiped build/_sdl3_install — restored afterwards via bootstrap-build.ps1); all 13 FDC/disk oracles green incl. the new `wd2793_write_stall` test. **Non-tautology + forensic match DEFINITIVE:** adversarial revert to the pre-M45 code reproduces the exact DEC-0067 signature (accurate-mode ONLY: 105 spurious zeros on the 12000-cyc stall, 316 on steady drift) and the 105-zero count lands inside the human's REAL corrupt `disk2.dsk` band (98/110/98/99 zeros at LBA 9/10/11/16 vs pristine `ys2-d2.dsk`) — proving the fix targets the actual corruption mechanism. BIOS-write byte-perfect (real BSAVE→DSKIO→WD2793, 512B + 2048B payloads byte-exact) and normal.dsk == fast.dsk BYTE-IDENTICAL → strict superset for the working case, mode-independent. `/WAIT` resolved (HB-F1XV does not wire FDC DRQ to CPU /WAIT; PhilipsFDC.cc:98-99). openMSX write A/B BLOCKED (interactive BSAVE hits DI;HALT/0 bytes — a harness issue, not the fix); QA judged acceptable for release because a `.dsk` is a flat logical-sector image (no gap/CRC/AM framing) so a well-behaved write yields sector==payload by construction — the proper end-to-end substitute is the owner live re-save (the CONDITION).
  **RESIDUAL (MEDIUM accuracy, non-blocking, backlogged):** the fix is CPU-paced — it commits every CPU byte (re-based edge handshake) and confines LOST_DATA to the first-byte CHECK_WRITE gate, so it NEVER substitutes 0x00 mid-transfer, whereas openMSX/the real WD2793 substitute 0x00+LOST_DATA on a genuinely-missed SCHEDULED tick. This is SAFER (a slow writer is preserved, never corrupted), INVISIBLE to all real software (real saves use DSKIO/DI/tight-poll → never miss a window), and consistent with our logical-.dsk architecture, but diverges from the letter of the spec in a pathological slow-writer case. Backlog: a full cycle-accurate scheduled-tick write model (analogous to the M44-Phase-2 CE-timing follow-on) for complete spec-parity — NOT needed for the human's data-integrity fix.
  **Repair:** the human's already-corrupt save is NOT recoverable (DEC-0067) — restore pristine `disks/games/ys2-pristine/ys2-d2.dsk` over `disks/games/ys2/disk2.dsk` (playable, save reverts to initial) OR re-save after the fix. Pending the human's OK to overwrite disk2.
- Impacted Milestones: **M45 → Done/CLOSED (QA CONDITIONAL PASS), tag target v1.1.1 @ `4a8f8e0` (owner-run + live re-save gate).** Local commits ahead of origin v1.0.40... actually origin/main = v1.1.0 @ `9f6eb8c`; the v1.1.1 tag will ship the unpushed chain: `561d32d` (README v1.1.0), `1a3e246` (arch diagram), `a27a1c4` (M44 Phase-1 foundation), `4a8f8e0` (M45 FDC write fix). Follow-on backlog: full cycle-accurate WD2793 write scheduled-tick model; M44 Phase-2 (CE-pacing); the pre-existing sprite-mode (sp2_double/sp3_collision) openMSX delta.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-12

- Decision ID: DEC-0070
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-12): live YS II in-game disk SAVE now HANGS the game (worse than the pre-fix corruption) — crash capture provided (debug/snapshot/stream_f001647_...: STATUS=04 LOST_DATA, DATA_INDEX=0, Type-I retry-seek loop).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator). Follow-up regression fix to DEC-0067/0068 (M45 FDC write). Universal + system-wide.
- Decision: **DEF-M45-WRITEDRQ-FIX — the M45 (`4a8f8e0`) WriteSector first-byte CHECK_WRITE gate window was FAR too short** (fixed `read_start_cycles()`=228 + 8-byte-period ~912 ≈ 1140 cycles), aborting YS II's legitimate save-buffer-then-write cadence with LOST_DATA writing nothing → game hang. On the real WD2793 the first data-byte DRQ is asserted only AFTER head-load + the ROTATIONAL sector-search (up to ~1 revolution) — a generous window; the read path already modeled this (begin_read_sector rotational latency) but the write path incorrectly used the fixed offset. FIX: `begin_write_sector` first-byte DRQ = `t + cycles_until_sector_id(...) + read_sector_header_cycles()` (rotational, same as read; --fast-disk collapses to t+32); CHECK_WRITE window = `drq_deadline_ + kWriteFirstByteWindowCycles` where kWriteFirstByteWindowCycles = kSystemClockHz/5 = 715909 (one 300rpm rev, NOT fast-scaled). Removed write_check_cycles()/kWriteCheckBytePeriods; added drq_deadline()/write_check_deadline() introspection accessors. **The M45 edge DRQ handshake + one-byte pipeline (the actual corruption fix) is KEPT INTACT** — only the first-byte window changed. openMSX-grounded (WD2793.cc:557,646-701,239 — understanding only, never copied). `src/devices/fdc/wd2793.{h,cpp}` ONLY, zero cpu/core → ZEXALL withheld-substituted (empty diff proven).
- Validation: fixed in an isolated worktree, cherry-picked to main (`0f648d7` over 572d9cc). NEW regression test devices_fdc_wd2793_write_firstbyte_unit_test (slow-first-byte 1500/8000/100000 cyc, both --fast-disk modes → completes, 512 bytes byte-exact, no LOST_DATA); **adversarial-revert proof: 21 assertions FAIL** on the old window (`completed=0 lost_data=1 bytes_written=0`) — non-tautological. type2 + write_stall re-derived to the rotational window (NOT weakened); M45 stall/corruption test + BSAVE round-trip stay byte-perfect. Combined main rebuild GREEN: build exit 0 (both exes), FDC/disk 15/15, full fast subset **222/222**.
- Impacted Milestones: M45 (write-path regression fix). **Final authoritative gate: the human's live YS II save-and-reload (with and without --fast-disk).** Bundles into v1.1.1.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-12

- Decision ID: DEC-0071
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-13, after v1.1.1 pushed): v1.1.2 = cosmetic + smarter-defaults enhancements ("system that works" convenience). Two design points confirmed via AskUserQuestion: (1) add a `--stock` escape hatch = YES; (2) FM-PAC auto-loads into SLOT 2 by default.

  1. **Defaults flipped (frontend default values, NOT the machine-constructor defaults):**
     - `--ram` default **512 KB** (was 64). `--ram 64` = stock. (S1985 5-bit ceiling per DEC-0061.)
     - `--fast-disk` default **ON** (was opt-in). New `--no-fast-disk` disables; Alt+D still toggles live.
     - **FM-PAC auto-loads into SLOT 2** by default (from `roms/fmpac.rom`), SRAM auto-persists to `roms/fmpac.rom.sram`. New `--no-fmpac` opts out; an explicit `--slot2 <rom>` overrides (user cart wins); **skipped gracefully (with a banner note) if `roms/fmpac.rom` is absent**. Rationale: "FM-PAC loaded whenever possible for its SRAM" — slot 2 lets a game cart in slot 1 coexist with FM-PAC.
  2. **`--stock` flag** — one-shot authentic bare machine (RAM 64 + accurate disk / no fast-disk + no FM-PAC). Explicit individual flags override `--stock` fields (precedence TBD by planner).
  3. **CLI rename `--cart1/--cart2` -> `--slot1/--slot2`** (+ `--cartN-type` -> `--slotN-type`), the official MSX hardware term. `--cartN`/`--cartN-type` KEPT as silent backward-compat aliases (existing scripts unbroken).
  4. **Banner "This session" enrichment:** VRAM (128 KB), FM-PAC status (loaded + which slot / not loaded / auto-load skipped), SRAM availability + path, RAM stock/modded, fast-disk, disk-writable, speed, scale/filter, `--stock` mode, and all active options.
- CRITICAL implementation risk (planner MUST address): flipping the FRONTEND defaults can silently drift the test/A-B baseline. The M42 default-64 byte-identity oracle + any test/tool that launches via CLI defaults + the openMSX A/B harness all assume bare-stock — they must be updated to pass explicit stock flags (or `--stock`) so the byte-identity + A/B parity guarantees are preserved under the new defaults. Machine-constructor defaults SHOULD stay stock so direct-construction tests are unaffected.
- Impacted Milestones: **M46 (opens).** Both executables (SDL3 + headless) get consistent defaults/flags. Files: `src/frontend/*` (CLI parse + banner) + `src/machine/*` (FM-PAC slot-2 auto-load wiring). Zero src/core & src/devices/cpu -> ZEXALL withheld-substituted. Acceptance: stock byte-identity preserved via `--ram 64`/`--stock`; FM-PAC slot-2 auto-load functional + SRAM persists + coexists with a slot-1 game; `--slotN` + `--cartN` aliases both work; banner accurate incl. the fmpac-absent path; A/B harness uses stock. Owner-run tag+push per DEC-0047.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-13

- Decision ID: DEC-0072
- Requested By: Human (2026-07-13): YS II in-game DISK saves STILL corrupt disk2 (sporadic; suspects saving to later save slots 1-8 on the already-inserted disk2). "100% sure this is FDC issue because saving to SRAM works 100%." Placed corrupted + pristine disk2 in games/disks/ys2/ (d2-corrupted.dsk / d2-pristine.dsk) + a pre-load debug snapshot. Authorized AUTONOMOUS run: "do investigate, build tools, run tests, fix codes, whatever it takes until QA passes... I will follow your recommendation, just keep running."
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator). Opens **M47** (autonomous, tag target v1.1.3). System-wide-review-first + universal-fixes (never game-specific).
- Decision: **DEF-M47-DISKWRITE — root-cause + eliminate the residual WD2793 disk-WRITE corruption once and for all.** Coordinator FORENSICS (games/disks/ys2/ d2-corrupted vs d2-pristine): EXACTLY 3 sectors differ — LBA 9, 15, 16 — each ALMOST WHOLLY wrong (510/482/507 of 512 bytes; 1499 total). The wrong data is COHERENT (not zeros, not a byte-shift of pristine) and is NOT found anywhere in the pristine image (external/save data, not a copy of a pristine sector); corrupted LBA 15 & 16 share their first ~158 bytes then diverge. YS II uses a CUSTOM (non-FAT12) disk layout, so treat sectors raw. The corrupted disk fails to LOAD the game (BGM still plays) → the trashed sectors are load-critical. **SRAM saves are byte-perfect → the game feeds CORRECT data; the corruption is purely in the emulator FDC disk-write path.** Leading hypotheses (to confirm): (a) SECTOR-ADDRESSING — write lands on the WRONG LBA (track/side/sector vs the working read path), esp. for higher tracks/sides = "later slots"; (b) MULTI-SECTOR (0xB0) buffer/advance bug — partial stale-buffer reuse across sectors (the LBA15/16 first-158-byte overlap) or wrong-sector continuation; (c) DRQ transfer_drq vs the S#1 DRQ status bit the CPU polls — a mismatch dropping/mis-committing bytes; (d) side-select/track-register staleness on write. Path: `wd2793.cpp` write_data(278)/begin_write_sector(487)/finish_write_sector(551) -> `drive_->write_sector(sector)` -> `DiskImage::chs_to_lba(track,side,sector)`/write_lba. References: openMSX WD2793.cc + fMSX WD1793.c/FDIDisk.c + WD279x datasheet (blueMSX NOT vendored -> use the two available + hardware spec + own analysis). `src/devices/fdc/*` (+ any bus/chipset/CPU seam the trace implicates); zero cpu/core expected -> ZEXALL withheld unless the trace forces a cpu/core edit.
- Impacted Milestones: **M47 (opens, autonomous).** Acceptance: reproduce the corruption signature headlessly (an FDC write-trace tool + a deterministic repro test), root-cause it, fix it UNIVERSALLY, and prove byte-perfect writes across ALL CHS (every track/side/sector), single + multi-sector (0xA0/0xB0), and adversarial CPU timing — the corruption signature GONE; full FDC/disk gate green; no read-path regression. Tag target v1.1.3, owner-run push per DEC-0047.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-13

- DEC-0072 OUTCOME (M47 fixed, 2026-07-13): commit `a27be57` (src/devices/fdc/wd2793 + disk_drive + machine stream-capture; ZERO cpu/core → empty diff proven, ZEXALL withheld). ROOT CAUSE (confirmed datasheet+openMSX+fMSX, docs/m47-fdc-write-investigation.md): `Wd2793::write_data` advanced the Write-Sector byte-position ONLY on `transfer_drq(t)` and SILENTLY DROPPED the byte otherwise → sector SHIFT under non-strictly-polled (early/burst/ISR-perturbed) cadences = the sporadic YS II save corruption (3 coherent-shifted side-1 sectors LBA 9/15/16). The M45 residual (its test only covered strict wait-for-DRQ). FIX (universal, real-WD2793 model): write_data LATCHES + commits the byte in-order ALWAYS (never dropped), decoupling byte-POSITION from CPU-write TIMING (re-base DRQ on actual service); un-serviced-slot 0x00+LostData substitution only on a full-revolution mid-transfer ABANDONMENT (never on poll/stall/burst); M45 first-byte CHECK_WRITE + rotational first-DRQ preserved; H4 = latch (track,side) at begin_write_sector, commit via DiskDrive::write_sector_at to the LATCHED CHS (a mid-transfer 0x7FFC side write can't redirect — all 3 corrupt sectors were side 1). New `wd2793_write_earlybyte` test (Cases A-H incl. 1440-sector all-CHS byte-perfect sweep) + non-tautology (QA's own revert: else-drop→11 fails+1440-CHS-wrong, H4-revert→Case E fails) + FdcSectorWriteObserver write-trace (stream_<id>_fdcwrite.log). QA **CONDITIONAL PASS** (docs/m47-qa-signoff.md): gates 71/71 + 144/144, M45 unchanged+green, read path byte-identical, deviation sound; LOW non-blockers only (Write-Track adversarial-test gap; slow-CPU LOST_DATA fidelity = M45 decision; owner-gated live trace). **v1.1.3 prepped — final gate = human live YS II re-save+reload BOTH --fast-disk modes (byte-trace via stream_<id>_fdcwrite.log).** Owner-run tag+push per DEC-0047.

- DEC-0072 CLOSED — FINAL VERDICT (M47, 2026-07-14): **the YS II 8-slot disk-save crash is INHERENT to the game/disk, NOT an emulator defect — the emulator is VINDICATED.** After the `a27be57` write-fix the owner's live 8-slot save STILL crashed on reload; a decisive independent test settled it: the identical save→load crash reproduces on the owner's LOCAL Windows openMSX (a separate accuracy-focused emulator) from a FRESH game on a VANILLA disk, across MULTIPLE game sources — two accurate emulators failing from a clean slate ⇒ the fault is the software on the disk (YS II's own save/load code mishandling a full 8-slot save area; the buggy routine is shared across the common crack lineage all these `.dsk` images descend from). EVIDENCE the FDC is byte-faithful: (1) an env-gated per-byte Write-Sector logger (`SONY_MSX_FDCWLOG`) over the deterministic replay = **0 substitutions**, byte stream **byte-identical** to what lands on disk (8 × 512 B, no drops/holes/overrun), corruption confined EXACTLY to the 8 save slots LBA 9-16 (no FAT/dir/adjacent spill → addressing is clean too); (2) an independent WD2793 datasheet audit — "no write-corruption defect exists in the FDC"; (3) openMSX itself immediately CRASHES loading OUR produced disk (`02f54bae`) — the bad data is created UPSTREAM of the FDC, when the game computes the save record from RAM. CORRECTION to an intermediate hypothesis: the crash IS timing-*sensitive* (a `--vdp-cmd-bias` sweep flips crash/no-crash on a cycle knife-edge), which tentatively reclassified this as "our CPU/VDP timing-fidelity bug" — but that was OVER-READ: openMSX runs at correct timing and STILL crashes, so correct timing does not avoid the crash; timing was a distraction, not the cause. The device-timing findings surfaced by the audit remain valid as independent correctness items (see DEC-0074) — they are NOT the YS II root cause. Crash mechanism (CPU trace): the loader reads the bad save, computes a garbage pointer, `SP` collapses `0xF202`→`0x4000` via an `LD SP,nn` on data, `RET` pops a garbage address → NOP-sled → `CALL M`/`0xFFFF`/`DI`/`0x0000 HALT` (final_pc=0x0001, terminal). Verdict doc: `docs/m47-dec0072-timing-fidelity-verdict.md`. Practical guidance for the owner: use 1-2 disk save slots (confirmed working) or FM-PAC SRAM saves (confirmed 100% reliable) — do not fill all 8 disk slots on these images. This CLOSES DEC-0072 / M47; no open emulator defect remains on the YS II track. The prior "DEC-0072 OUTCOME (M47 fixed)" entry above is superseded on the *cause* question (the write model is a kept improvement, not the fix that mattered).

- Decision ID: DEC-0073
- Requested By: Coordinator (2026-07-14), grounded in the mission "as genuine to real Sony HB-F1XV / MSX2+ hardware as possible" and surfaced concretely by the DEC-0072/M47 CPU interrupt-timing reference disagreement (our fact-sheet guessed 14T but deferred to openMSX; signal-level hardware reasoning + a bare-Z80 ⇒ 13T).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator). Standing directive; governs ALL future behavior/timing grounding.
- Decision: **REFERENCE PRECEDENCE (authority order — STRICT, non-negotiable).** When grounding any hardware behavior or timing decision, weigh sources in this order and prefer the higher tier; never silently resolve a conflict:
  1. **Real-hardware specification (HIGHEST — final authority).** Authoritative datasheets / hardware documentation for the actual silicon (Z80A, V9958, S1985/YM2149, YM2413/OPLL, RP-5C01, WD2793, …), whether curated in `references/fact-sheets/` or sourced via primary/community hardware documentation. The real-hardware spec is the final word on what is correct.
  2. **openMSX + own spec-disciplined reasoning.** A mature, years-refined behavior reference and the basis for A/B parity — the strong default where the hardware spec is silent or ambiguous — but its long evolution may carry modeling tweaks that do NOT match real hardware. When openMSX conflicts with an authoritative hardware spec, **the spec wins** and the divergence is documented (report/decision) rather than followed.
  3. **fMSX (LOWEST).** An independent implementation lineage; use only to triangulate when tiers 1 and 2 are unavailable or disagree.
  openMSX A/B remains the parity harness; a confirmed hardware conflict resolves in favor of hardware, with the openMSX divergence documented rather than followed. This DEMOTES the prior "openMSX = primary/authoritative behavior reference" framing to tier 2.
- Propagation (done this session): CLAUDE.md + all 5 `.claude/agents/*.md` + all 5 `.claude/commands/*.md` + `agent-protocol/project-baseline.md` (§"Reference Precedence (Authority Order — Strict, Non-Negotiable)") + `agent-protocol/guardrails.md` (reference-precedence rule).
- Impacted Milestones: standing (all future). First applied in DEC-0074 (the CPU 13T resolution: tier-1 hardware reasoning led, openMSX A/B confirmed as tier-2 corroboration).
- Effective Date: 2026-07-14

- Decision ID: DEC-0074
- Requested By: Coordinator (2026-07-14) — the 4-specialist device-fidelity audit run during the DEC-0072/M47 investigation surfaced three real, independently-grounded correctness defects (distinct from the YS II crash, which is game/disk per DEC-0072).
- Approved By: MSX Master Agent (coordinator). Universal, system-wide, spec-modeling fixes (never game-specific) under the reference-precedence directive (DEC-0073).
- Decision: **CPU / VDP / PSG timing-parity fixes (verified).**
  1. **CPU interrupt/NMI-acknowledge timing.** The S1985 +1 M1 wait does NOT apply to the interrupt/NMI-ack M1 — it gates on the opcode-fetch (/M1 + /MREQ), not the acknowledge cycle (/M1 + /IORQ). Corrected: **IM1 = 13T, IM2 = 19T, NMI = 11T** (were 14/20/12). Tier-1 grounded (signal-level reasoning + bare-Z80 timing + MSX community), with a live openMSX A/B measured as tier-2 confirmation. Implemented via a `tick_refresh_only()` split (the ack ticks R but not the M1-wait counter) + an NMI R-tick fix; 4 test oracles updated (`interrupt_ack`, `cpu_parity`, `cpu_bootstrap_im1`, `m23_halt_r`); `references/fact-sheets/Zilog Z80A CPU.md` §5 corrected. This is the single most systematic prior timing drift (fired on every VBlank/line interrupt).
  2. **V9958 command-engine timing.** LINE per-pixel 88→112 (+32 for the minor Bresenham step); per-line end-of-line overhead added (HMMV +56, HMMM +64, LMMV +64, LMMM +64, YMMM +0); LMCM/LMMC/HMMC transfer-ready (TR) now per-unit paced (never drops data). Tier-1 grounded (fact-sheet §8 logic-analyzer cost table). The bug was matching openMSX's deliberate `calcFinishTime` UNDER-estimate rather than its real execution timing. The full access-slot CONTENTION model (154/88/31 slots + CPU↔command slot stealing) is DEFERRED — HIGH risk and license-sensitive ~340-entry tables (the standing C1/D4 UNBUILDABLE-WITHOUT-FABRICATION ban, `feedback_license_sensitive_scope.md`).
  3. **PSG (YM2149).** Tone/Noise counter clamps to period-1 on a period-shrinking write (was reset to 0), matching openMSX `Generator::setPeriod` and our own `Envelope::set_period` (no reference disagreement). Audio-fidelity only; no game-logic impact.
- Validation: full deterministic suite **228/228** including the ZEXALL/ZEXDOC sweep after the CPU-core work (the direct-cpu-edit sweep trigger per `feedback_slow_test_cadence.md`); the VDP suite green after the VDP work.
- Impacted Milestones: M47 (device-fidelity hardening alongside the DEC-0072 closure). `src/devices/cpu/*`, `src/devices/video/*`, `src/devices/audio/psg_ym2149.*`. Version/tag/push are the owner's call per DEC-0047.
- Effective Date: 2026-07-14
